<p><b>McGill University</b> (<a href="/wiki/French_language" title="French language">French</a>: <i lang="fr">Université McGill</i>) is a <a href="/wiki/Public_university" title="Public university">public</a> <a href="/wiki/Research_university" title="Research university">research university</a> in <a href="/wiki/Montreal" title="Montreal">Montreal</a>, <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>, Canada. It was established in 1821 by <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a>, granted by <a href="/wiki/George_IV_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George IV of the United Kingdom">King George IV</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Frost,_Stanley_Brice_1895_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frost,_Stanley_Brice_1895-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> The university bears the name of <a href="/wiki/James_McGill" title="James McGill">James McGill</a>, a Montreal merchant originally from Scotland whose bequest in 1813 formed the university's precursor, McGill College.
</p><p>McGill's main campus is located at <a href="/wiki/Mount_Royal" title="Mount Royal">Mount Royal</a> in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Montreal" title="Downtown Montreal">downtown Montreal</a>, with the <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_Campus" title="Macdonald Campus">second campus</a> situated in <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue,_Quebec" title="Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue, Quebec">Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue</a>, also on the Montreal Island, 30 kilometres (18 miles) west of the main campus. The university is one of two universities outside the United States who are members of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a><sup id="cite_ref-8" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-8">&#91;8&#93;</a></sup> and it is the only Canadian member of the <a href="/wiki/Global_University_Leaders_Forum" title="Global University Leaders Forum">Global University Leaders Forum</a> (GULF) within the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-McGill_newsroom_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGill_newsroom-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>McGill offers degrees and diplomas in over 300 fields of study, with the highest average admission requirements of any Canadian university.<sup id="cite_ref-entering_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entering-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Most students are enrolled in the five largest faculties, namely <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill University Faculty of Arts">Arts</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Science" title="McGill University Faculty of Science">Science</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Medicine" title="McGill University Faculty of Medicine">Medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Engineering" title="McGill University Faculty of Engineering">Engineering</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Desautels_Faculty_of_Management" title="Desautels Faculty of Management">Management</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Enrolment_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enrolment-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>McGill counts among its alumni <a href="/wiki/List_of_Nobel_laureates_by_university_affiliation" title="List of Nobel laureates by university affiliation">12 Nobel laureates</a> and 144 <a href="/wiki/Rhodes_Scholars" class="mw-redirect" title="Rhodes Scholars">Rhodes Scholars</a>, both the most of any university in Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">&#91;12&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13">&#91;13&#93;</a></sup> as well as five astronauts,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">&#91;14&#93;</a></sup> three <a href="/wiki/Canadian_prime_ministers" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian prime ministers">Canadian prime ministers</a>, the incumbent <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>, 14 justices of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Canadian Supreme Court</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">&#91;15&#93;</a></sup> four <a href="/wiki/Leader" class="mw-redirect" title="Leader">foreign leaders</a>, 28 foreign ambassadors, nine <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> (Oscars) winners, 11 <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winners, four <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners,<sup id="cite_ref-PP1_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PP1-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PP2_17-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PP2-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup> at least 16 <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Award" title="Emmy Award">Emmy Award</a> winners,<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">&#91;18&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19">&#91;19&#93;</a></sup> and 28 <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> medalists, all of varying nationalities. McGill alumni were instrumental in inventing or initially organizing <a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">football</a>, <a href="/wiki/Basketball" title="Basketball">basketball</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">ice hockey</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lennox2009_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lennox2009-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup>  McGill University or its alumni also founded several major universities and colleges, including the Universities of <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia" title="University of British Columbia">British Columbia</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Victoria" title="University of Victoria">Victoria</a>, and <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta" title="University of Alberta">Alberta</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Schulich_School_of_Medicine_%26_Dentistry" title="Schulich School of Medicine &amp; Dentistry">Schulich School of Medicine &amp; Dentistry</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">Johns Hopkins University School of Medicine</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Dawson_College" title="Dawson College">Dawson College</a>.
</p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Royal_Institution_for_the_Advancement_of_Learning">Royal Institution for the Advancement of Learning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Royal Institution for the Advancement of Learning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The Royal Institution for the Advancement of Learning (RIAL) was created in 1801 under an Act of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Lower_Canada" title="Legislative Assembly of Lower Canada">Legislative Assembly of Lower Canada</a>, <i>An Act for the establishment of Free Schools and the Advancement of Learning in this Province</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">&#91;21&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1816 the RIAL was authorized to operate two new Royal Grammar Schools, in Quebec City and in Montreal. This was a turning point for public education in Lower Canada as the schools were created by legislation, the District Public Schools Act of 1807, which showed the government's willingness to support the costs of education and even the salary of a schoolmaster. This was an important first step in the creation of nondenominational schools. When James McGill died in 1813 his bequest was administered by the RIAL.
</p><p>Of the original two Royal Grammar Schools, in 1846 one closed and the other merged with the <a href="/wiki/High_School_of_Montreal" title="High School of Montreal">High School of Montreal</a>. By the mid-19th century the RIAL had lost control of the other eighty-two <a href="/wiki/Grammar_schools" class="mw-redirect" title="Grammar schools">grammar schools</a> it had administered.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">&#91;22&#93;</a></sup> However, in 1853 it took over the High School of Montreal from the school's Board of Directors and continued to operate it until 1870.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">&#91;23&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24">&#91;24&#93;</a></sup> Thereafter, its sole remaining purpose was to administer the McGill bequest on behalf of the private college. The RIAL continues to exist today; it is the <a href="/wiki/Corporate_identity" title="Corporate identity">corporate identity</a> that runs the university and its various constituent bodies, including the former Macdonald College (now Macdonald Campus), the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Neurological_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Montreal Neurological Institute">Montreal Neurological Institute</a>, and the Royal Victoria College (the former women's college turned residence). Since the revised Royal Charter of 1852, The Trustees of the RIAL comprise the Board of Governors of McGill University.<sup id="cite_ref-Frost,_Stanley_Brice_1895_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frost,_Stanley_Brice_1895-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="McGill_College">McGill College</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: McGill College">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:James_McGill.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/James_McGill.jpg/170px-James_McGill.jpg" width="170" height="219" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/James_McGill.jpg/255px-James_McGill.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/83/James_McGill.jpg/340px-James_McGill.jpg 2x" data-file-width="593" data-file-height="765" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:James_McGill.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/James_McGill" title="James McGill">James McGill</a>, the original <a href="/wiki/Benefactor_(law)" title="Benefactor (law)">benefactor</a> of McGill University.</div></div></div> <p><a href="/wiki/James_McGill" title="James McGill">James McGill</a>, born in <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a>, Scotland on 6 October 1744, was a successful merchant in Quebec, having matriculated into the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a> in 1756.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">&#91;25&#93;</a></sup> Between 1811 and 1813,<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">&#91;26&#93;</a></sup> he drew up a will leaving his "Burnside estate", a 19-hectare (47-acre) tract of <a href="/wiki/Rural" class="mw-redirect" title="Rural">rural</a> land and 10,000 <a href="/wiki/Pound_sterling" title="Pound sterling">pounds</a> to the Royal Institution for the Advancement of Learning.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">&#91;27&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">&#91;28&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-Kip_29-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kip-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On McGill's death in December 1813, the Royal Institution for the Advancement of Learning, established in 1801 by an Act of the <a href="/wiki/Legislative_Assembly_of_Lower_Canada" title="Legislative Assembly of Lower Canada">Legislative Assembly of Lower Canada</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-charter_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> added the establishing of a University pursuant to the conditions of McGill's will to its original function of administering <a href="/wiki/Elementary_education" class="mw-redirect" title="Elementary education">elementary education</a> in <a href="/wiki/Lower_Canada" title="Lower Canada">Lower Canada</a>.
</p><p>As a condition of the bequest, the land and funds had to be used for the establishment of a "University or College, for the purposes of Education and the Advancement of Learning in the said Province."<sup id="cite_ref-charter_30-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-charter-30">&#91;30&#93;</a></sup> The will specified that a private, constituent college<sup id="cite_ref-Frost,_Stanley_Brice_1895_7-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Frost,_Stanley_Brice_1895-7">&#91;7&#93;</a></sup> bearing his name would have to be established within 10 years of his death; otherwise the bequest would revert to the heirs of his wife.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">&#91;31&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 31, 1821, after protracted <a href="/wiki/Legal_battle" class="mw-redirect" title="Legal battle">legal battles</a> with the Desrivières family (the heirs of his wife), McGill College received a <a href="/wiki/Royal_charter" title="Royal charter">royal charter</a> from <a href="/wiki/George_IV_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="George IV of the United Kingdom">King George IV</a>. The Charter provided that the College should be deemed and taken as a <a href="/wiki/University" title="University">University</a>, with the power of conferring <a href="/wiki/Academic_degree" title="Academic degree">degrees</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">&#91;32&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_development">University development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: University development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_expansions">Campus expansions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Campus expansions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_William_Dawson_1884.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Sir_William_Dawson_1884.jpg/170px-Sir_William_Dawson_1884.jpg" width="170" height="248" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Sir_William_Dawson_1884.jpg/255px-Sir_William_Dawson_1884.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/52/Sir_William_Dawson_1884.jpg/340px-Sir_William_Dawson_1884.jpg 2x" data-file-width="517" data-file-height="754" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_William_Dawson_1884.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Sir John William Dawson, Principal of McGill University, 1855–1893</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg/220px-McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg" width="220" height="107" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg/330px-McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/0f/McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg/440px-McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3872" data-file-height="1884" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_Arts_Building2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Arts Building, completed in 1843 and designed by <a href="/wiki/John_Ostell" title="John Ostell">John Ostell</a>, is the oldest building on campus.</div></div></div>
<p>Although McGill College received its Royal Charter in 1821, it was inactive until 1829 when the Montreal Medical Institution, which had been founded in 1823, became the college's first academic unit and Canada's first medical school. The Faculty of Medicine granted its first degree, a Doctorate of Medicine and Surgery, in 1833; this was also the first medical degree to be awarded in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33">&#91;33&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Faculty of Medicine remained the school's only functioning faculty until 1843, when the Faculty of Arts commenced teaching in the newly constructed Arts Building and East Wing (Dawson Hall).<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">&#91;34&#93;</a></sup> The university also historically has strong links with the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Grenadier_Guards" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian Grenadier Guards">Canadian Grenadier Guards</a>, a military regiment in which James McGill served as Lieutenant-Colonel. This title is marked upon the stone that stands before the Arts building, from where the Guards step off annually to commemorate Remembrance Day.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Dawson_Gallery_-_Redpath_Museum_-_McGill_University_-_Montreal,_Canada_-_DSC07893.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Dawson_Gallery_-_Redpath_Museum_-_McGill_University_-_Montreal%2C_Canada_-_DSC07893.jpg/220px-Dawson_Gallery_-_Redpath_Museum_-_McGill_University_-_Montreal%2C_Canada_-_DSC07893.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Dawson_Gallery_-_Redpath_Museum_-_McGill_University_-_Montreal%2C_Canada_-_DSC07893.jpg/330px-Dawson_Gallery_-_Redpath_Museum_-_McGill_University_-_Montreal%2C_Canada_-_DSC07893.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Dawson_Gallery_-_Redpath_Museum_-_McGill_University_-_Montreal%2C_Canada_-_DSC07893.jpg/440px-Dawson_Gallery_-_Redpath_Museum_-_McGill_University_-_Montreal%2C_Canada_-_DSC07893.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5472" data-file-height="3648" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Dawson_Gallery_-_Redpath_Museum_-_McGill_University_-_Montreal,_Canada_-_DSC07893.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The interior of the <a href="/wiki/Redpath_Museum" title="Redpath Museum">Redpath Museum</a></div></div></div>
<p>The Faculty of Law was founded in 1848 which is also the oldest of its kind in the nation. 48 years later, the school of architecture at McGill University was founded.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">&#91;35&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/John_William_Dawson" title="John William Dawson">Sir John William Dawson</a>, McGill's principal from 1855 to 1893, is often credited with transforming the school into a modern university.<sup id="cite_ref-transformation_36-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-transformation-36">&#91;36&#93;</a></sup> He recruited the aid of Montreal's wealthiest citizens (eighty percent of Canada's wealth was then controlled by families who lived within the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Square_Mile" title="Golden Square Mile">Golden Square Mile</a> area that surrounded the university), many of whom donated property and funding needed to construct the campus buildings. Their names adorn many of the campus's prominent buildings.
</p><p>William Spier designed the
addition of West Wing of the Arts Building for William Molson, 1861.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">&#91;37&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Francis_Dunlop" title="Alexander Francis Dunlop">Alexander Francis Dunlop</a> designed major alterations to the East Wing of McGill College (now called the Arts Building, McGill University) for Prof. Bovey and the Science Dept., 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">&#91;38&#93;</a></sup> This expansion of the campus continued until 1920. Buildings designed by <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Taylor_(Architect)" class="mw-redirect" title="Andrew Taylor (Architect)">Andrew Taylor</a>, include the <a href="/wiki/Redpath_Museum" title="Redpath Museum">Redpath Museum</a> (1880), <a href="/w/index.php?title=Macdonald_Physics_Building&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Macdonald Physics Building (page does not exist)">Macdonald Physics Building</a> (1893), the <a href="/wiki/Redpath_Library" class="mw-redirect" title="Redpath Library">Redpath Library</a> (1893), the Macdonald Chemistry Building (1896), the Macdonald Engineering Building (1907)—now known as the Macdonald-Stewart Library Building, and the Strathcona Medical Building (1907)—since renamed the Strathcona Anatomy and Dentistry Building.
</p><p>In 1900, the university established the MacLennan Travelling Library. <i>McGill University Waltz</i> composed by Frances C. Robinson, was published in Montréal by W.H. Scroggie, c 1904.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">&#91;39&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal,_Montreal_(HS85-10-17321).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg/300px-McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg" width="300" height="144" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg/450px-McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7a/McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg/600px-McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal%2C_Montreal_%28HS85-10-17321%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1686" data-file-height="808" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_University_and_Mount_Royal,_Montreal_(HS85-10-17321).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>McGill University and Mount Royal, 1906, Panoramic Photo Company</div></div></div><p> In 1885, the university's Board of Governors formally adopted the use of the name "McGill University". In 1905, the university acquired a second campus when <a href="/wiki/William_Christopher_Macdonald" title="William Christopher Macdonald">Sir William C. Macdonald</a>, one of the university's major benefactors, endowed a college in Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue, 32 kilometres west of Montreal. Macdonald College, now known as the <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_Campus" title="Macdonald Campus">Macdonald Campus</a>, opened to students in 1907, originally offering programs in agriculture, household science, and teaching.
</p><p>George Allan Ross designed the Pathology Building, 1922–23; the Neurological Institute, 1933; Neurological Institute addition 1938 at McGill University.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">&#91;40&#93;</a></sup> Jean Julien Perrault (architect) designed the <a href="/wiki/McTavish_Street" title="McTavish Street">McTavish Street</a> residence for Charles E. Gravel, which is now called David Thompson House (1934).<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">&#91;41&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span id="Women.27s_education"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Women's_education">Women's education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Women&#039;s education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>Women's education at McGill began in 1884, when <a href="/wiki/Donald_Smith,_1st_Baron_Strathcona_and_Mount_Royal" title="Donald Smith, 1st Baron Strathcona and Mount Royal">Donald Smith</a>  (later the <a href="/wiki/Baron_Strathcona_and_Mount_Royal" title="Baron Strathcona and Mount Royal">Lord Strathcona and Mount Royal</a>), began funding separate lectures for women, given by university staff members. The first degrees granted to women at McGill were conferred in 1888.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">&#91;42&#93;</a></sup> In 1899, the Royal Victoria College (RVC) opened as a residential college for women at McGill with <a href="/wiki/Hilda_D._Oakeley" title="Hilda D. Oakeley">Hilda D. Oakeley</a> as the head. Until the 1970s, all female undergraduate students, known as "Donaldas," were considered to be members of RVC.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">&#91;43&#93;</a></sup> Beginning in the autumn of 2010, the newer Tower section of Royal Victoria College is a <i>co-ed</i> dormitory, whereas the older West Wing remains strictly for women. Both the Tower and the West Wing of Royal Victoria College form part of the university's residence system.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="McGill_in_the_Great_War">McGill in the Great War</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: McGill in the Great War">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg/220px-2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg" width="220" height="83" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg/330px-2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d1/2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg/440px-2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4852" data-file-height="1825" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:2nd_University_Company_at_McGill_1915.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Second University Company prior to their departure for France.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_University,_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg/220px-McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg" width="220" height="224" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c6/McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg/330px-McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/c/c6/McGill_University%2C_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg 2x" data-file-width="437" data-file-height="444" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_University,_Stained_Glass_War_Memorial.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Stained Glass Great War Memorial entrance to the Blackader-Lauterman Library of Architecture and Art</div></div></div>
<p>McGill University played a significant role in the Great War. Many students and alumni enlisted in the first wave of patriotic fervor that swept the nation in 1914, but in the spring of 1915—after the first wave of heavy Canadian casualties at Ypres—Hamilton Gault, the founder of the Canadian regiment and a wealthy Montreal businessman, was faced with a desperate shortage of troops. When he reached out to his friends at home for support, over two hundred were commissioned from the ranks, and many more would serve as soldiers throughout the war. On their return to Canada after the war, Major George McDonald and Major George Currie formed the accounting firm McDonald Currie, which later became one of the founders of <a href="/wiki/PricewaterhouseCoopers" title="PricewaterhouseCoopers">Price Waterhouse Coopers</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">&#91;44&#93;</a></sup> Captain <a href="/wiki/Percival_Molson" title="Percival Molson">Percival Molson</a> was killed in action in July 1917. <a href="/wiki/Percival_Molson_Memorial_Stadium" title="Percival Molson Memorial Stadium">Percival Molson Memorial Stadium</a> at McGill is named in his honour.
</p><p>The War Memorial Hall (more generally known as Memorial Hall) is a landmark building on the campus of McGill University. At the dedication ceremony the Governor General of Canada (<a href="/wiki/Harold_Alexander,_1st_Earl_Alexander_of_Tunis" title="Harold Alexander, 1st Earl Alexander of Tunis">Harold Alexander, 1st Earl Alexander of Tunis</a>) laid the cornerstone. Dedicated on October 6, 1946, the Memorial Hall and adjoining Memorial Pool honour students who had enlisted and died in the <a href="/wiki/First_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="First World War">First World War</a>, and in the <a href="/wiki/Second_World_War" class="mw-redirect" title="Second World War">Second World War</a>. In Memorial Hall, there are two Stained Glass Regimental badge World War I and World War II Memorial Windows by <a href="/wiki/Charles_William_Kelsey" title="Charles William Kelsey">Charles William Kelsey</a> c. 1950/1.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">&#91;45&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>A war memorial window (1950) by <a href="/wiki/Charles_William_Kelsey" title="Charles William Kelsey">Charles William Kelsey</a> in the McGill War Memorial Hall depicts the figure of St. Michael and the badges of the Navy, Army and the Air Force.
A Great War memorial window featuring Saint George and a slain dragon at the entrance to the Blackader-Lauterman Library of Architecture and Art is dedicated to the memory of 23 members of the McGill Chapter of <a href="/wiki/Delta_Upsilon" title="Delta Upsilon">Delta Upsilon</a> who gave their lives in the Great War.<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">&#91;46&#93;</a></sup>
Six other windows (1951) by <a href="/wiki/Charles_William_Kelsey" title="Charles William Kelsey">Charles William Kelsey</a> on the west wall of the memorial hall depict the coats of arms of the regiments in which the McGill alumni were members.
</p><p>There is a memorial archway at <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_College" class="mw-redirect" title="Macdonald College">Macdonald College</a>, two additional floors added to the existing <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Currie" title="Arthur Currie">Sir Arthur Currie</a> gymnasium, a hockey rink and funding for an annual Memorial Assembly. A Book of Remembrance on a marble table contains the names of those lost in both World Wars. On 11 November 2012 the McGill Remembers web site launched; the University War Records Office collected documents between 1940–1946 related to McGill students, staff and faculty in the Second World War.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">&#91;47&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Quotas_on_Jewish_students">Quotas on Jewish students</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Quotas on Jewish students">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Beginning in the 1920, and continuing until the 1960s, McGill imposed a controversial quota which specified a maximum on the proportion of newly admitted students who were Jewish. The quota limited the Jewish population across McGill to at most 10%.<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48">&#91;48&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Founder_of_universities_and_colleges">Founder of universities and colleges</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Founder of universities and colleges">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>McGill was instrumental in founding several major universities and colleges. It established the first post-secondary institutions in <a href="/wiki/British_Columbia" title="British Columbia">British Columbia</a> to provide degree programs to the growing cities of <a href="/wiki/Vancouver" title="Vancouver">Vancouver</a> and <a href="/wiki/Victoria,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria, British Columbia">Victoria</a>. It chartered <a href="/wiki/Victoria_College,_British_Columbia" title="Victoria College, British Columbia">Victoria College</a> in 1903 as an affiliated junior college of McGill, offering first and second-year courses in arts and science, until it became today's <a href="/wiki/University_of_Victoria" title="University of Victoria">University of Victoria</a>. British Columbia's first university was incorporated in Vancouver in 1908 as the <a href="/wiki/University_of_British_Columbia" title="University of British Columbia">McGill University College of British Columbia</a>. The private institution granted McGill degrees until it became the independent University of British Columbia in 1915.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">&#91;49&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Dawson_College" title="Dawson College">Dawson College</a> began in 1945 as a satellite campus of McGill to absorb the anticipated influx of students after <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">World War II</a>. Many students in their first 3 years in the Faculty of Engineering took courses at Dawson College to relieve the McGill campus for the later two years for their degree course. Dawson eventually became independent of McGill and evolved into the first English <a href="/wiki/CEGEP" title="CEGEP">CEGEP</a> in <a href="/wiki/Quebec" title="Quebec">Quebec</a>. Another CEGEP, <a href="/wiki/John_Abbott_College" title="John Abbott College">John Abbott College</a>, was established in 1971 at the campus of McGill's Macdonald College.
</p><p>Both founders of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Alberta" title="University of Alberta">University of Alberta</a>, Premier <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Cameron_Rutherford" title="Alexander Cameron Rutherford">Alexander Cameron Rutherford</a> of Alberta and <a href="/wiki/Henry_Marshall_Tory" title="Henry Marshall Tory">Henry Marshall Tory</a>, were also McGill alumni. In addition, McGill alumni and professors, <a href="/wiki/William_Osler" title="William Osler">Sir William Osler</a> and <a href="/wiki/Howard_Atwood_Kelly" title="Howard Atwood Kelly">Howard Atwood Kelly</a>, were among the four founders and early faculty members of the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">Johns Hopkins University School of Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50">&#91;50&#93;</a></sup> Osler eventually became the first Physician-in-Chief of the new <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_Hospital" title="Johns Hopkins Hospital">Johns Hopkins Hospital</a> in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore</a>, Maryland, US in 1889. He led the creation of the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_University_School_of_Medicine" class="mw-redirect" title="Johns Hopkins University School of Medicine">Johns Hopkins University School of Medicine</a> in 1893.  Other McGill alumni founded the <a href="/wiki/Schulich_School_of_Medicine_%26_Dentistry" title="Schulich School of Medicine &amp; Dentistry">Schulich School of Medicine &amp; Dentistry</a> in the 1880s.
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus">Campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McTavish_Street,_Montreal_07.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/McTavish_Street%2C_Montreal_07.jpg/220px-McTavish_Street%2C_Montreal_07.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/McTavish_Street%2C_Montreal_07.jpg/330px-McTavish_Street%2C_Montreal_07.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1e/McTavish_Street%2C_Montreal_07.jpg/440px-McTavish_Street%2C_Montreal_07.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McTavish_Street,_Montreal_07.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The recently renovated <a href="/wiki/McTavish_Street" title="McTavish Street">McTavish street</a> is a critical artery connecting the lower campus to the upper campus.</div></div></div>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Downtown_campus">Downtown campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Downtown campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg/220px-Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg" width="220" height="164" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg/330px-Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4f/Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg/440px-Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg 2x" data-file-width="760" data-file-height="565" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Ice_hockey_McGill_University_1884.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A hockey game on campus in 1884, just seven years after McGill students wrote the then-new game's first rule book, with the Arts Building, Redpath Museum, and Morrice Hall (then the Presbyterian College) visible.</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_Campus_Twilight.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/24/McGill_Campus_Twilight.jpg/220px-McGill_Campus_Twilight.jpg" width="220" height="82" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/24/McGill_Campus_Twilight.jpg/330px-McGill_Campus_Twilight.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/2/24/McGill_Campus_Twilight.jpg/440px-McGill_Campus_Twilight.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3860" data-file-height="1440" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_Campus_Twilight.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>McGill's downtown campus at night viewed from <a href="/wiki/Mount_Royal" title="Mount Royal">Mount Royal</a>. The circular building in the foreground is the McIntyre Medical Sciences Building.</div></div></div>
<p>McGill's main campus is situated in <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Montreal" title="Downtown Montreal">downtown Montreal</a> at the foot of <a href="/wiki/Mount_Royal" title="Mount Royal">Mount Royal</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51">&#91;51&#93;</a></sup> Most of its buildings are situated in a park-like campus (also known as the Lower Campus) located north of <a href="/wiki/Sherbrooke_Street" title="Sherbrooke Street">Sherbrooke Street</a> and south of <a href="/wiki/Pine_Avenue" title="Pine Avenue">Pine Avenue</a> between <a href="/wiki/Peel_Street,_Montreal" title="Peel Street, Montreal">Peel</a> and Aylmer streets. The campus also extends west of Peel Street (also known as Upper Campus) for several blocks, starting north of <a href="/wiki/Doctor_Penfield_Avenue" title="Doctor Penfield Avenue">Doctor Penfield</a>; the campus also extends east of <a href="/wiki/University_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="University Street">University Street</a>, starting north of Pine Avenue, an area that includes McGill's <a href="/wiki/Percival_Molson_Memorial_Stadium" title="Percival Molson Memorial Stadium">Percival Molson Memorial Stadium</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Neurological_Institute_and_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Montreal Neurological Institute and Hospital">Montreal Neurological Institute and Hospital</a>. The community immediately east of University Street and south of Pine Avenue is known as the <a href="/wiki/McGill_Ghetto" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill Ghetto">McGill Ghetto</a>, where a large number of students reside. The campus is near the <a href="/wiki/Peel_(Montreal_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Peel (Montreal Metro)">Peel</a> and <a href="/wiki/McGill_(Montreal_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill (Montreal Metro)">McGill</a> <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Metro" title="Montreal Metro">Metro</a> stations. A major downtown boulevard, <a href="/wiki/McGill_College_Avenue" title="McGill College Avenue">McGill College Avenue</a>, leads up to the Roddick Gates, the university's formal main entrance. All of the major university buildings were constructed using local grey <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">limestone</a>, which serves as a unifying element.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">&#91;52&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The university's first classes were held in at Burnside Place, James McGill's country home.<sup id="cite_ref-Kip_29-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Kip-29">&#91;29&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">&#91;53&#93;</a></sup> Burnside Place remained the sole educational facility until the 1840s, when the school began construction on its first buildings: the central and east wings of the Arts Building.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">&#91;54&#93;</a></sup> The rest of the campus was essentially a cow <a href="/wiki/Pasture" title="Pasture">pasture</a>, a situation similar to the few other Canadian universities and early American colleges of the age.<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">&#91;55&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The university's athletic facilities, including <a href="/wiki/Molson_Stadium" class="mw-redirect" title="Molson Stadium">Molson Stadium</a>, are located on Mount Royal, near the residence halls and the Montreal Neurological Institute. The Gymnasium is named in honour of General <a href="/wiki/Sir_Arthur_William_Currie" class="mw-redirect" title="Sir Arthur William Currie">Sir Arthur William Currie</a>.
</p><p>In 2012, <i><a href="/wiki/Travel_%2B_Leisure" title="Travel + Leisure">Travel + Leisure</a></i> rated McGill's campus as one of the 17 most beautiful university campuses in the world.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">&#91;56&#93;</a></sup>
</p>

			<div class="thumb" style="width: 150px;"><div style="margin:30px auto;"><a href="/wiki/File:Roddick_Gates_(McGill_University)_2005-09-02.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Roddick_Gates_%28McGill_University%29_2005-09-02.jpg/120px-Roddick_Gates_%28McGill_University%29_2005-09-02.jpg" width="120" height="90" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Roddick_Gates_%28McGill_University%29_2005-09-02.jpg/180px-Roddick_Gates_%28McGill_University%29_2005-09-02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e8/Roddick_Gates_%28McGill_University%29_2005-09-02.jpg/240px-Roddick_Gates_%28McGill_University%29_2005-09-02.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a></div></div>

</p>
			</div>

<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Residence">Residence</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Residence">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Street_of_the_Ghetto_McGill,_Montreal_2005-08-30.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Street_of_the_Ghetto_McGill%2C_Montreal_2005-08-30.jpg/220px-Street_of_the_Ghetto_McGill%2C_Montreal_2005-08-30.jpg" width="220" height="118" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Street_of_the_Ghetto_McGill%2C_Montreal_2005-08-30.jpg/330px-Street_of_the_Ghetto_McGill%2C_Montreal_2005-08-30.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/ba/Street_of_the_Ghetto_McGill%2C_Montreal_2005-08-30.jpg/440px-Street_of_the_Ghetto_McGill%2C_Montreal_2005-08-30.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2546" data-file-height="1365" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Street_of_the_Ghetto_McGill,_Montreal_2005-08-30.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The "McGill Ghetto"</div></div></div>
<p>McGill's residence system houses approximately 3,100 undergraduate students and some graduate students.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57">&#91;57&#93;</a></sup> With the exception of students returning as "floor fellows" or "<a href="/wiki/Resident_assistant" title="Resident assistant">dons</a>", few McGill students live in <a href="/wiki/Dormitory" title="Dormitory">residence</a> (known <a href="/wiki/Colloquialism" title="Colloquialism">colloquially</a> as "rez") after their first year of undergraduate study, even if they are not from the Montreal area. Most second-year students transition to off-campus apartment housing. Many students settle in the "<a href="/wiki/McGill_Ghetto" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill Ghetto">McGill Ghetto</a>", alternatively known as the Milton-Park community, the neighbourhood directly to the east of the downtown campus. In recent years, students have begun moving out to other areas such as Mile End, The Plateau, and even as far as Verdun because of rising rent prices.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">&#91;58&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many first-year students live in the Bishop Mountain Residences ("Upper Rez"),<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">&#91;59&#93;</a></sup> a series of concrete dormitories on the slope of Mount Royal, consisting of McConnell Hall, Molson Hall, Gardner Hall, and Douglas Hall. McGill's largest residence is New Residence Hall ("New Rez"), a converted four-star hotel located a few blocks east of campus at <a href="/wiki/Park_Avenue_(Montreal)" title="Park Avenue (Montreal)">Park Avenue</a> and Prince Arthur. It houses approximately 700 students each year. Solin Hall, located near <a href="/wiki/Lionel-Groulx_(Montreal_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Lionel-Groulx (Montreal Metro)">Lionel-Groulx station</a>, is McGill's second largest residence, housing roughly 300 students. Carrefour Sherbrooke Residence Hall was opened in 2009 on 475 Sherbrooke Street West, previously the Four Points Sheraton Hotel. In 2012, McGill opened La Citadelle, a converted hotel residence housing 286 students located on Sherbrooke Street West at the corner of Hutchinson.
</p><p>Royal Victoria College, once a women-only dormitory, became co-ed in September 2010. The college's original building was designed by <a href="/wiki/Bruce_Price" title="Bruce Price">Bruce Price</a> and its extension was designed by <a href="/wiki/Percy_Erskine_Nobbs" title="Percy Erskine Nobbs">Percy Erskine Nobbs</a> and George Taylor Hyde.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">&#91;60&#93;</a></sup> Erected in front of the Royal Victoria College is a statue of <a href="/wiki/Queen_Victoria" title="Queen Victoria">Queen Victoria</a> by her daughter <a href="/wiki/Princess_Louise,_Duchess_of_Argyll" title="Princess Louise, Duchess of Argyll">Princess Louise, Duchess of Argyll</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">&#91;61&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Solin_Hall_-_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Solin_Hall_-_01.jpg/220px-Solin_Hall_-_01.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Solin_Hall_-_01.jpg/330px-Solin_Hall_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/9c/Solin_Hall_-_01.jpg/440px-Solin_Hall_-_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Solin_Hall_-_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Solin Hall, situated in <a href="/wiki/Saint-Henri,_Montreal" title="Saint-Henri, Montreal">Saint-Henri</a> near <a href="/wiki/Lionel-Groulx_station" title="Lionel-Groulx station">Lionel-Groulx Station</a>, serves as an off-campus apartment style dorm.</div></div></div>
<p>Among the <i>McGill Off-Campus Residence Experience</i> buildings are Presbyterian Hall ("Pres Rez"), adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/The_Presbyterian_College,_Montreal" title="The Presbyterian College, Montreal">Presbyterian College</a>, and University Hall (also known as "Dio"), adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Diocesan_Theological_College" title="Montreal Diocesan Theological College">Montreal Diocesan Theological College</a>. Greenbriar Hall houses 89 students. Other buildings included in the <i>McGill Off-Campus Residence Experience</i> are located on <a href="/wiki/Peel_Street,_Montreal" title="Peel Street, Montreal">Peel Street</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_Street" class="mw-redirect" title="University Street">University Street</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Pine_Avenue" title="Pine Avenue">Pine Avenue</a>, however, the university has begun the process of selling off buildings as now only University Hall and some <a href="/wiki/Pine_Avenue" title="Pine Avenue">Pine Avenue</a> houses are left.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Macdonald_campus">Macdonald campus</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Macdonald campus">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_Campus" title="Macdonald Campus">Macdonald Campus</a></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MacdonaldCollege1906.gif" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/MacdonaldCollege1906.gif/220px-MacdonaldCollege1906.gif" width="220" height="124" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/MacdonaldCollege1906.gif/330px-MacdonaldCollege1906.gif 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/MacdonaldCollege1906.gif/440px-MacdonaldCollege1906.gif 2x" data-file-width="640" data-file-height="360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MacdonaldCollege1906.gif" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Macdonald Campus under construction in 1906</div></div></div>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McGillMacDonaldArms.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/64/McGillMacDonaldArms.png/220px-McGillMacDonaldArms.png" width="220" height="220" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/64/McGillMacDonaldArms.png/330px-McGillMacDonaldArms.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/6/64/McGillMacDonaldArms.png/440px-McGillMacDonaldArms.png 2x" data-file-width="1200" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McGillMacDonaldArms.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Macdonald Campus coat of arms</div></div></div>
<p>A second campus, the <a href="/wiki/Macdonald_Campus" title="Macdonald Campus">Macdonald Campus</a>, in <a href="/wiki/Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue,_Quebec" title="Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue, Quebec">Sainte-Anne-de-Bellevue</a> houses the Faculty of Agricultural and Environmental Science, the School of Dietetics and Human Nutrition, the Institute of Parasitology, and the McGill School of Environment. The <a href="/wiki/Morgan_Arboretum" title="Morgan Arboretum">Morgan Arboretum</a> and the <a href="/wiki/J._S._Marshall_Radar_Observatory" title="J. S. Marshall Radar Observatory">J. S. Marshall Radar Observatory</a> are nearby.
</p><p>The Morgan <a href="/wiki/Arboretum" title="Arboretum">Arboretum</a> was created in 1945. It is a 2.5-square-kilometre (0.965&#160;sq&#160;mi) forested reserve with the aim of 'teaching, research, and public education'. Its mandated research goals are to continue research related to maintaining the health of the Arboretum <a href="/wiki/Plantations" class="mw-redirect" title="Plantations">plantations</a> and <a href="/wiki/Woodland" title="Woodland">woodlands</a>, to develop new programs related to selecting <a href="/wiki/Species" title="Species">species</a> <a href="/wiki/Adaptation" title="Adaptation">adapted</a> to developing environmental conditions and to develop silvicultural practices that preserve and enhance <a href="/wiki/Biodiversity" title="Biodiversity">biological diversity</a> in both natural stands and plantations.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">&#91;62&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="McGill_University_Health_Centre_redevelopment_plan">McGill University Health Centre redevelopment plan</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: McGill University Health Centre redevelopment plan">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2006, the Quebec government initiated a $1.6 billion <a href="/wiki/Leadership_in_Energy_and_Environmental_Design" title="Leadership in Energy and Environmental Design">LEED</a> redevelopment project for the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Health_Centre" title="McGill University Health Centre">McGill University Health Centre</a> (MUHC). The project will expand facilities to two separate campuses<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63">&#91;63&#93;</a></sup> and consolidate the various hospitals of the MUHC on the site of an old <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Pacific_Railway" title="Canadian Pacific Railway">CP</a> <a href="/wiki/Rail_yard" title="Rail yard">rail yard</a> adjacent to the <a href="/wiki/Vend%C3%B4me_(Montreal_Metro)" class="mw-redirect" title="Vendôme (Montreal Metro)">Vendôme</a> <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Metro" title="Montreal Metro">Metro</a> station. This site, known as Glen Yards, comprises 170,000 square metres (1,800,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) and spans portions of Montreal's <a href="/wiki/Notre-Dame-de-Gr%C3%A2ce" title="Notre-Dame-de-Grâce">Notre-Dame-de-Grâce</a> neighbourhood and the city of <a href="/wiki/Westmount,_Quebec" title="Westmount, Quebec">Westmount</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">&#91;64&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The Glen Yards project has been controversial due to local opposition to the project, environmental issues, and the cost of the project itself.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65">&#91;65&#93;</a></sup> The project, which has received approval from the provincial government, was, in 2003, expected to be complete by 2010. The new 'campus' has now been completed, and a massive effort of moving units from older hospitals, such <a href="/wiki/Royal_Victoria_Hospital,_Montreal" title="Royal Victoria Hospital, Montreal">Royal Victoria</a>, <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Montreal Children&#39;s Hospital">Montreal Children's</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Montreal_General_Hospital" title="Montreal General Hospital">Montreal General</a>, into the new McGill University Health Center is underway.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sustainability">Sustainability</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Sustainability">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 2007, McGill premiered its Office of Sustainability and added a second full-time position in this area, the Director of Sustainability in addition to the Sustainability Officer.<sup id="cite_ref-Sustainability_66-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainability-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Recent efforts in implementing its sustainable development plan include the new Life Sciences Center which was built with LEED-Silver certification and a green roof, as well as an increase in parking rates in January 2008 to fund other sustainability projects.<sup id="cite_ref-Sustainability_66-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Sustainability-66">&#91;66&#93;</a></sup> Other student projects include The Flat: Bike Collective, which promotes alternative transportation, and the Farmer's Market, which occurs during the fall harvest.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_Sustainability:_Campus_Committees_and_Groups_67-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_Sustainability:_Campus_Committees_and_Groups-67">&#91;67&#93;</a></sup> The Farmer's Market and many other initiatives came out of student collaboration during the Rethink Conference 2008.<sup id="cite_ref-Office_of_Sustainability:_Rethink_Forms_68-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Office_of_Sustainability:_Rethink_Forms-68">&#91;68&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Other_facilities">Other facilities</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Other facilities">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:MUHC_Superhospital_(May_2015).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/MUHC_Superhospital_%28May_2015%29.jpg/220px-MUHC_Superhospital_%28May_2015%29.jpg" width="220" height="95" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/MUHC_Superhospital_%28May_2015%29.jpg/330px-MUHC_Superhospital_%28May_2015%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/62/MUHC_Superhospital_%28May_2015%29.jpg/440px-MUHC_Superhospital_%28May_2015%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3264" data-file-height="1415" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:MUHC_Superhospital_(May_2015).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The newly built <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Health_Centre" title="McGill University Health Centre">McGill University Health Centre</a> at the Glen Site</div></div></div>
<p>McGill's <a href="/wiki/Bellairs_Research_Institute" title="Bellairs Research Institute">Bellairs Research Institute</a>, located in <a href="/wiki/Saint_James,_Barbados" title="Saint James, Barbados">Saint James, Barbados</a> <span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=McGill_University&amp;params=13_10_N_59_35_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">13°10′N</span> <span class="longitude">59°35′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">13.167°N 59.583°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">13.167; -59.583</span></span></span></a></span>, is Canada's only teaching and research facility in the tropics.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">&#91;69&#93;</a></sup> The institute has been in use for over 50 years.
</p><p>The laboratories of the <a href="/wiki/Huntsman_Marine_Science_Centre" title="Huntsman Marine Science Centre">Huntsman Marine Science Centre</a> are located in <a href="/wiki/St._Andrews,_New_Brunswick" title="St. Andrews, New Brunswick">St. Andrews, N.B.</a>, on 300,000 square metres (3,200,000&#160;sq&#160;ft) of land at the <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">estuary</a> of the <a href="/wiki/St._Croix_River_(Maine-New_Brunswick)" class="mw-redirect" title="St. Croix River (Maine-New Brunswick)">St. Croix River</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70">&#91;70&#93;</a></sup> It hosts the Atlantic Reference Centre, which is known throughout the <a href="/wiki/Maritimes" title="Maritimes">Maritimes</a> for its extensive marine biology collections.<sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71">&#91;71&#93;</a></sup> The HMS is a research facility "committed to the advancement of the marine sciences through basic and applied research"<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">&#91;72&#93;</a></sup> and acts as a field facility for research and teaching by McGill and other member universities.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Rutherford_Park,_Montreal_03.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rutherford_Park%2C_Montreal_03.jpg/220px-Rutherford_Park%2C_Montreal_03.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rutherford_Park%2C_Montreal_03.jpg/330px-Rutherford_Park%2C_Montreal_03.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8d/Rutherford_Park%2C_Montreal_03.jpg/440px-Rutherford_Park%2C_Montreal_03.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5184" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Rutherford_Park,_Montreal_03.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Rutherford_Park" class="mw-redirect" title="Rutherford Park">Parc Rutherford</a> at night. The Genome Building (left), Wong Building (middle), and McTavish Reservoir (right) are seen in the background.</div></div></div>
<p>McGill's Gault <a href="/wiki/Nature_Reserve" class="mw-redirect" title="Nature Reserve">Nature Reserve</a> (<span class="plainlinks nourlexpansion"><a class="external text" href="//tools.wmflabs.org/geohack/geohack.php?pagename=McGill_University&amp;params=45_32_N_73_10_W_"><span class="geo-default"><span class="geo-dms" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location"><span class="latitude">45°32′N</span> <span class="longitude">73°10′W</span></span></span><span class="geo-multi-punct">&#xfeff; / &#xfeff;</span><span class="geo-nondefault"><span class="geo-dec" title="Maps, aerial photos, and other data for this location">45.533°N 73.167°W</span><span style="display:none">&#xfeff; / <span class="geo">45.533; -73.167</span></span></span></a></span>) spans over 10 square kilometres (3.9&#160;sq&#160;mi) of forest land, the largest remaining remnant of the <a href="/wiki/Old_growth_forest" class="mw-redirect" title="Old growth forest">primeval forests</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Saint_Lawrence_River" title="Saint Lawrence River">St. Lawrence River Valley</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">&#91;73&#93;</a></sup> The first scientific studies at the site occurred in 1859. The site has been the site of extensive research activities:
"Today there are over 400 scientific articles, 100 graduate theses, more than 50 government reports and about 30 book chapters that are based on research at <a href="/wiki/Mont-Saint-Hilaire,_Quebec" title="Mont-Saint-Hilaire, Quebec">Mont St. Hilaire</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-74" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-74">&#91;74&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In addition to the McGill University Health Centre, McGill has been directly partnered with many <a href="/wiki/Teaching_hospital" title="Teaching hospital">teaching hospitals</a> for decades, and also has a history of collaborating with many hospitals in Montreal. These cooperations allow the university to graduate over 1,000 students in <a href="/wiki/Health_care" title="Health care">health care</a> each year.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">&#91;75&#93;</a></sup> McGill's contract-affiliated teaching hospitals include the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Children%27s_Hospital" title="Montreal Children&#39;s Hospital">Montreal Children's Hospital</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_General_Hospital" title="Montreal General Hospital">Montreal General Hospital</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Neurological_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Montreal Neurological Hospital">Montreal Neurological Hospital</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Chest_Institute" title="Montreal Chest Institute">Montreal Chest Institute</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Royal_Victoria_Hospital,_Montreal" title="Royal Victoria Hospital, Montreal">Royal Victoria Hospital</a> which are all now part of the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Health_Centre" title="McGill University Health Centre">McGill University Health Centre</a>. Other hospitals that health care students may use include the <a href="/wiki/Jewish_General_Hospital" title="Jewish General Hospital">Jewish General Hospital</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Douglas_Hospital" class="mw-redirect" title="Douglas Hospital">Douglas Hospital</a> and <a href="/wiki/St._Mary%27s_Hospital_(Montreal)" title="St. Mary&#39;s Hospital (Montreal)">St. Mary's Hospital Center</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">&#91;76&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Until the late 19th century, McGill had also owned parkland atop the <a href="/wiki/Westmount_Summit" title="Westmount Summit">Westmount Summit</a>, which was used as a <a href="/wiki/Botanical_garden" title="Botanical garden">botanical garden</a>. In the early twentieth century, McGill donated the land to the <a href="/wiki/City_of_Westmount" class="mw-redirect" title="City of Westmount">City of Westmount</a> on the condition that it become a <a href="/wiki/Bird_sanctuary" class="mw-redirect" title="Bird sanctuary">bird sanctuary</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Les_amis_77-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Les_amis-77">&#91;77&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 1998, the Faculty of Management launched their <a href="/wiki/Desautels_Faculty_of_Management#MBA" title="Desautels Faculty of Management">MBA Japan</a> program, the first Canadian degree program offered in <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">Japan</a>, with teaching facilities at <a href="/wiki/Nishi-Shinjuku" title="Nishi-Shinjuku">Nishi-Shinjuku</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tokyo" title="Tokyo">Tokyo</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">&#91;78&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Administration_and_organization">Administration and organization</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Administration and organization">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Structure">Structure</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Structure">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
