<p>The University's academic units are organized into 11 main Faculties and Schools.<sup id="cite_ref-FS_79-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FS-79">&#91;79&#93;</a></sup> These include the School of Architecture, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_School_of_Computer_Science" title="McGill University School of Computer Science">School of Computer Science</a>, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_School_of_Information_Studies" title="McGill University School of Information Studies">School of Information Studies</a>, the School of Dietetics and Human Nutrition, the School of Physical &amp; Occupational Therapy, the Ingram School of Nursing, the School of Social Work, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_%E2%80%93_School_of_Urban_Planning" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill University – School of Urban Planning">School of Urban Planning</a>, and the McGill School of Environment. They also include the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Institute_of_Islamic_Studies" title="McGill University Institute of Islamic Studies">Institute of Islamic Studies</a> (established in 1952) which offers graduate courses leading to the M.A. and Ph.D. degrees, and covering the history, culture, and civilization of Islam; the Institute is also served by one of the richest libraries in North America on Islamic studies.
</p><p>The Graduate and Postdoctoral Studies<sup id="cite_ref-gps_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-gps-80">&#91;80&#93;</a></sup> (GPS) oversees the admission and registration of graduate students (both master's and Ph.D.). The GPS administers graduate fellowships, postdoctoral affairs, and the graduation process, including the examination of theses. In conjunction with other units, it conducts regular program reviews in all study disciplines.
</p><p>Founded in 1956, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_Executive_Institute" title="McGill Executive Institute">McGill Executive Institute</a> provides business seminars and custom executive education to companies, government services and non-profit organizations. Led primarily by McGill faculty, the executive courses and management training programs are designed for all managerial levels, from board members to senior-level executives to junior managers.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="University_identity_and_culture">University identity and culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: University identity and culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:173px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Mcgill_CoA.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/5/5b/Mcgill_CoA.jpg" width="171" height="206" class="thumbimage" data-file-width="171" data-file-height="206" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Mcgill_CoA.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>McGill’s <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a></div></div></div>
<p>The McGill <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">coat of arms</a> is derived from an armorial device assumed during his lifetime by the founder of the University, James McGill. The University's patent of arms was granted by the <a href="/wiki/Garter_Principal_King_of_Arms" title="Garter Principal King of Arms">Garter King at Arms</a> in 1922, registered in 1956 with <a href="/wiki/Lord_Lyon_King_of_Arms" title="Lord Lyon King of Arms">Lord Lyon King of Arms</a> in Edinburgh, and in 1992 with the <a href="/wiki/Public_Register_of_Arms,_Flags_and_Badges_of_Canada" title="Public Register of Arms, Flags and Badges of Canada">Public Register of Arms, Flags and Badges of Canada</a>. In heraldic terms, the coat of arms is described as follows: "Argent three Martlets Gules, on a chief dancette of the second, an open book proper garnished or bearing the legend <i>In Domino Confido</i> in letters Sable between two crowns of the first. Motto: <i>Grandescunt Aucta Labore</i>." The coat of arms consists of two parts, the shield and the scroll. The University publishes a guide to the use of the University's arms and motto.<sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">&#91;81&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The University's symbol is the <a href="/wiki/Martlet" title="Martlet">martlet</a>, stemming from the presence of the mythical bird on the official <a href="/wiki/Coat_of_arms" title="Coat of arms">arms</a> of the university. The university's official colour is scarlet, which figures prominently in the <a href="/wiki/Academic_dress_of_McGill_University" title="Academic dress of McGill University">academic dress of McGill University</a>. McGill's motto is <i>Grandescunt Aucta Labore</i>, <a href="/wiki/Latin_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Latin language">Latin</a> for "By work, all things increase and grow" (literally, "Things grown great increase by work," that is, things that grow to be great do so by means of work). The official <a href="/wiki/School_song" title="School song">school song</a> is entitled "Hail, <a href="/wiki/Alma_Mater" class="mw-redirect" title="Alma Mater">Alma Mater</a>."<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">&#91;82&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="International_student_life">International student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: International student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>McGill hosts around 500 incoming exchange students from over 32 countries. The university offers a multitude of activities and events to integrate the students in the university's community as well as to introduce them to the North American academic culture.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Finances">Finances</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Finances">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>As a public university, McGill is not as dependent on its endowment for operating revenue as some of its international peers. The McGill endowment only provides approximately 10 per cent of the school's annual operating revenues.<sup id="cite_ref-mcgill.ca_83-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgill.ca-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Nonetheless, McGill's endowment rests within the top 10 percent of all North American post-secondary institutions' endowments.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">&#91;84&#93;</a></sup> While McGill's conservative investment policy has protected it from the more substantial losses experienced at many other universities during the market crisis of 2008–2009, it still faced a 20% endowment decline from approximately $920 million to $740 million.<sup id="cite_ref-mcgill.ca_83-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgill.ca-83">&#91;83&#93;</a></sup> Currently valued at $39,881 per student, the university's endowment is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_Canadian_universities_by_endowment" title="List of Canadian universities by endowment">largest among Canadian universities</a> on a per-student basis.
</p><p>McGill launched the <i>Campaign McGill</i> comprehensive campaign in October 2007,<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">&#91;85&#93;</a></sup> with the goal of raising over $750 million for the purpose of further "attracting and retaining top talent in Quebec, to increase access to quality education and to further enhance McGill's ability to address critical global problems."<sup id="cite_ref-History_in_the_Making_86-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_in_the_Making-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup> The largest goal of any Canadian university fundraising campaign in history,<sup id="cite_ref-History_in_the_Making_86-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-History_in_the_Making-86">&#91;86&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">&#91;87&#93;</a></sup> within the first six months, McGill had accumulated over $400 million towards its efforts.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">&#91;88&#93;</a></sup>
The campaign was officially closed on 18 June 2013.<sup id="cite_ref-The_Globe_and_Mail_89-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-The_Globe_and_Mail-89">&#91;89&#93;</a></sup> The university surpassed its initial goal of $750 million and raised more than $1 billion.<sup id="cite_ref-Montreal_Gazette_90-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Montreal_Gazette-90">&#91;90&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Academics">Academics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Academics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Admissions">Admissions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Admissions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Twenty-two percent of all students are enrolled in the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Arts" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill University Faculty of Arts">Faculty of Arts</a>, McGill's largest academic unit. Of the other larger faculties, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Science" title="McGill University Faculty of Science">Faculty of Science</a> enrolls 15%, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Medicine" title="McGill University Faculty of Medicine">Faculty of Medicine</a> enrolls 13%, the School of Continuing Studies enrolls 12%, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Engineering" title="McGill University Faculty of Engineering">Faculty of Engineering</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Desautels_Faculty_of_Management" title="Desautels Faculty of Management">Desautels Faculty of Management</a> enroll about 10% each.<sup id="cite_ref-Enrolment_11-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Enrolment-11">&#91;11&#93;</a></sup> The remainder of all students are enrolled in McGill's smaller schools, including the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Agricultural_and_Environmental_Sciences" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill University Faculty of Agricultural and Environmental Sciences">Faculty of Agricultural and Environmental Sciences</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Dentistry" title="McGill University Faculty of Dentistry">Faculty of Dentistry</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Education" title="McGill University Faculty of Education">Faculty of Education</a>, <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Law" title="McGill University Faculty of Law">Faculty of Law</a>, <a href="/wiki/Schulich_School_of_Music" title="Schulich School of Music">Schulich School of Music</a>, and the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Religious_Studies" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill University Faculty of Religious Studies">Faculty of Religious Studies</a>. Since the 1880s,<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">&#91;91&#93;</a></sup> McGill has been affiliated with three <a href="/wiki/Seminary" title="Seminary">Theological Colleges</a>; the <a href="/wiki/Anglican_Diocese_of_Montreal" title="Anglican Diocese of Montreal">Montreal Diocesan</a> Theological College (<a href="/wiki/Anglican_Church_of_Canada" title="Anglican Church of Canada">Anglican Church of Canada</a>), <a href="/wiki/The_Presbyterian_College,_Montreal" title="The Presbyterian College, Montreal">The Presbyterian College, Montreal</a> (<a href="/wiki/Presbyterian_Church_in_Canada" title="Presbyterian Church in Canada">Presbyterian Church in Canada</a>), and United Theological College (<a href="/wiki/United_Church_of_Canada" title="United Church of Canada">United Church of Canada</a>).<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">&#91;92&#93;</a></sup> The university's Faculty of Religious Studies maintains additional affiliations with other theological institutions and organizations, such as the Montreal School of Theology.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">&#91;93&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017, the university offered admission to 15,771 students out of a total of 36,304 undergraduate applicants with 6,467 students enrolling.<sup id="cite_ref-94" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-94">&#91;94&#93;</a></sup> McGill students have the highest average entering grade of any Canadian university.<sup id="cite_ref-entering_10-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-entering-10">&#91;10&#93;</a></sup> Among admitted students, the median Quebec <a href="/wiki/CEGEP" title="CEGEP">CEGEP</a> <a href="/wiki/R-score" class="mw-redirect" title="R-score">R-score</a> was 30.0, while the median grade 12 averages for students entering McGill from outside of Quebec ranged between 92% and 93% (A). For American students, the median <a href="/wiki/SAT" title="SAT">SAT</a> scores in the verbal, mathematics, and writing sections were 700, 690, and 710 respectively, for a combined SAT score of around 2100; the median <a href="/wiki/ACT_(test)" title="ACT (test)">ACT</a> score was 31.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Due to its bilingual nature, McGill's law school does not require applicants to sit the <a href="/wiki/Law_School_Admission_Test" title="Law School Admission Test">LSAT</a>, stating that, "it would be disadvantageous to the significant proportion of applicants and admitted students who indicate French as a first language to require, as a matter of eligibility, a test that is offered only in English." For students who submitted LSAT scores in the September 2017 entering class the median LSAT score was 162 (86.8th percentile) out of a possible 180 points. Of those students who entered with a bachelor's degree the median GPA was 84%, and of those students entering from CEGEP the average R-score was 33.8.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup> For medical students, the median undergraduate GPA was 3.83 out of 4.0.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> McGill does not require applicants to its medical programme who have an undergraduate degree from a Canadian university to sit the <a href="/wiki/Medical_College_Admission_Test" title="Medical College Admission Test">MCAT</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> In the Desautels Faculty of Management's MBA program, applicants had an average <a href="/wiki/Graduate_Management_Admission_Test" title="Graduate Management Admission Test">GMAT</a> score of 670 and an average GPA of 3.3.<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> MBA students had an average age of 28, and five years of work experience. 95% of MBA students are bilingual and 60% are trilingual.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Teaching_and_learning">Teaching and learning</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Teaching and learning">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In the 2007–2008 school year, McGill offered over 340 academic programs in eleven faculties.<sup id="cite_ref-students_5-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-students-5">&#91;5&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The university also offers over 250 doctoral and master's graduate degree programs. Despite strong increases in university enrollment across North America,<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup> McGill has upheld a relatively low and appealing student-faculty ratio of 16:1.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> There are nearly 1,600 <a href="/wiki/Tenure" class="mw-redirect" title="Tenure">tenured</a> or tenure-track professors teaching at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-facultystaff_4-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-facultystaff-4">&#91;4&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Tuition" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuition">Tuition fees</a> vary significantly between in-<a href="/wiki/Provinces_and_territories_of_Canada" title="Provinces and territories of Canada">province</a>, out-of-province, and international students, with full-time Quebec students paying around $4,014.82<sup id="cite_ref-admissions_costs_at_mcgill.ca_105-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admissions_costs_at_mcgill.ca-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> per year, Canadian students from other provinces paying around $8,799.82<sup id="cite_ref-admissions_costs_at_mcgill.ca_105-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admissions_costs_at_mcgill.ca-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> per year, and <a href="/wiki/Canadian_nationality_law" title="Canadian nationality law">international</a> students paying $18,267.22–$41,815.92 per year.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Students must also pay housing costs, though Montreal has some of the least expensive housing among large North American cities.
</p><p>Since 1996, McGill, in accordance with the <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Education,_Recreation_and_Sports_(Quebec)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Education, Recreation and Sports (Quebec)">Quebec Ministry of Education, Recreation and Sports</a> (Ministère de l'Éducation, du Loisir et du Sport or MELS), has had eight categories that qualifies certain international students to be excused from paying international fees. These categories include: students from France, a quota of students from select countries which have agreements with MELS, which include <a href="/wiki/Algeria" title="Algeria">Algeria</a>, China, and <a href="/wiki/Morocco" title="Morocco">Morocco</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup> students holding diplomatic status, including their <a href="/wiki/Dependent_(law)" class="mw-redirect" title="Dependent (law)">dependents</a>, and students enrolled in certain language programs leading to a degree in French.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup>
In the school year 2008–2009, McGill's graduate business program became funded by tuition, and was the last business school in Canada to do so.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Scholarships" class="mw-redirect" title="Scholarships">Scholarships</a> at McGill are relatively difficult to attain, compared to other Canadian universities.<sup id="cite_ref-scholar1_110-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scholar1-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-scholar2_111-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scholar2-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-scholar3_112-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scholar3-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-scholar4_113-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-scholar4-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> For out-of-province first year undergraduate students, a high school average of 95% is required to receive a guaranteed one-year entrance scholarship.<sup id="cite_ref-Entrance_114-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Entrance-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> To be considered for the same scholarships, Quebec CEGEP students need a minimum R-score of 35.5, United States high school students need a minimum A average as well as at least 700 in each SAT or 33 in the ACT, and French Baccalaureate students need an average of 15.5 plus a minimum score of 14 in each course; similarly, students in the British education system need As in both GCSE Level and predicted Advanced Level results, and International Baccalaureate students need to attain a minimum overall average of 6.9 on predicted grades or a score of 42 on exam results. In general, entrance scholarship recipients rank in the top 1–2% of their class.
</p><p>For renewal of previously earned scholarships, students generally need to be within the top 10% of their faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> For in-course scholarships in particular, students must be within the top 5% of their faculty.<sup id="cite_ref-incoursescholarships_116-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-incoursescholarships-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-deanshonourlist_117-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-deanshonourlist-117">&#91;117&#93;</a></sup> McGill itself outlines scholarship considerations as follows: "Competition for basic and major scholarships is intense at McGill. An extraordinary number of exceptional applications are received each year and therefore we cannot award scholarships to all good candidates."<sup id="cite_ref-Entrance_114-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Entrance-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The university has joined Project Hero, a scholarship program cofounded by General (Ret'd) <a href="/wiki/Rick_Hillier" title="Rick Hillier">Rick Hillier</a> for the families of fallen <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Forces" class="mw-redirect" title="Canadian Forces">Canadian Forces</a> members.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">&#91;118&#93;</a></sup> McGill is also partnered with the <a href="/wiki/STEM_fields" class="mw-redirect" title="STEM fields">STEM</a> initiative <a href="/wiki/Schulich_Leader_Scholarships" title="Schulich Leader Scholarships">Schulich Leader Scholarships</a>, awarding an $80,000 scholarship to an incoming engineering student and a $60,000 scholarship to a student pursuing a degree in science/technology/mathematics each year.<sup id="cite_ref-Schulich_119-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Schulich-119">&#91;119&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Language_policy">Language policy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Language policy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>McGill is one of three English-language universities in Quebec;  French is not a requirement to attend. The Faculty of Law does, however, require all students to be "passively bilingual", meaning that all students must be able to understand written and spoken French—or English if the student is Francophone—since English or French may be used at any time in a course. Over 38,000<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">&#91;120&#93;</a></sup> students attend McGill, with international students comprising one-fifth of the student population. The majority of students are fluent in at least two languages.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">&#91;121&#93;</a></sup> Francophone students, whether from Quebec or overseas, now make up approximately 18 percent of the student body.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">&#91;122&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Although the language of instruction is English, since its founding McGill has allowed students to write their thesis in French, and since 1964 students in all faculties have been able to submit any graded work in either English or French, provided that the objective of the class is not to learn a particular language.<sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">&#91;123&#93;</a></sup> The University has a bilingual language policy and charter.
</p><p>In 1969, the <a href="/wiki/Quebec_nationalism" title="Quebec nationalism">nationalist</a> <i>McGill français</i> movement demanded that McGill become francophone, pro-nationalist, and pro-worker.<sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">&#91;124&#93;</a></sup> The movement was led by Stanley Gray, a <a href="/wiki/Political_science" title="Political science">political science</a> <a href="/wiki/Professor" title="Professor">professor</a> (and possibly unaware of government plans after the recent (1968) legislation founding the <a href="/wiki/Universit%C3%A9_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Université du Québec">Université du Québec</a>)<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">&#91;125&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">&#91;126&#93;</a></sup> A demonstration was held of 10,000 trade unionists, leftist activists, CEGEP students, and even some McGill students, at the university's <a href="/wiki/Roddick_Gates" title="Roddick Gates">Roddick Gates</a> on March 28, 1969. Protesters saw English as the privileged language of commerce. McGill, where <a href="/wiki/Francophone" class="mw-redirect" title="Francophone">Francophones</a> comprised only three percent of the students, could be seen as the force maintaining economic control by <a href="/wiki/English-speaking_Quebecker" class="mw-redirect" title="English-speaking Quebecker">Anglophones</a> of a predominantly French-speaking province.<sup id="cite_ref-127" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-127">&#91;127&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">&#91;128&#93;</a></sup> However, the majority of students and faculty opposed such a position.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">&#91;129&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">&#91;130&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rankings_and_reputation">Rankings and reputation</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Rankings and reputation">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="infobox" style="width:22em;width:23em; font-size:80%"><tbody><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center;font-size:125%;font-weight:bold"><a href="/wiki/Rankings_of_universities_in_Canada" title="Rankings of universities in Canada">University rankings</a></th></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Global rankings</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">ARWU</a></i> World<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_131-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-ARWUCAND_132-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-ARWUCAND-132">&#91;132&#93;</a></sup></th><td>
70</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS</a></i> World<sup id="cite_ref-QS_133-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup></th><td>

44</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i> Reputation<sup id="cite_ref-UnivRankings_THES_REP_135-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnivRankings_THES_REP-135">&#91;135&#93;</a></sup></th><td>
41</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i> Employability<sup id="cite_ref-UnivRankings_THES_GEUR_136-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnivRankings_THES_GEUR-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup></th><td>
18</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/U.S_News_%26_World_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S News &amp; World Report">U.S News &amp; World Report</a></i> Global<sup id="cite_ref-USNWR_Best_Global_Universities_137-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR_Best_Global_Universities-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup></th><td>
49</td></tr><tr><th colspan="2" style="text-align:center">Canadian rankings</th></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/College_and_university_rankings#Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="College and university rankings">ARWU</a></i> National<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_131-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup></th><td>
3</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS</a></i> National<sup id="cite_ref-QS_133-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup></th><td>
2</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times</a></i> National<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_134-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup></th><td>
3</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/U.S_News_%26_World_Report" class="mw-redirect" title="U.S News &amp; World Report">U.S News &amp; World Report</a></i> National<sup id="cite_ref-USNWR_Best_Global_Universities_137-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USNWR_Best_Global_Universities-137">&#91;137&#93;</a></sup></th><td>
3</td></tr><tr><th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s#University_Ranking_Guide" title="Maclean&#39;s">Maclean's</a></i> Medical/Doctoral<sup id="cite_ref-Macdoc_138-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Macdoc-138">&#91;138&#93;</a></sup></th><td>
1</td></tr></tbody></table>
<p>As of the 2017–2018 school year, McGill is ranked 1st in Canada among all its major/research universities in the <i><a href="/wiki/Maclean%27s" title="Maclean&#39;s">Maclean's</a></i> 24th annual rankings, maintaining this position for the 12th consecutive year.<sup id="cite_ref-Maclean_139-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Maclean-139">&#91;139&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Internationally, McGill ranked 33rd in the world and second in Canada in the 2019 <a href="/wiki/QS_World_University_Rankings" title="QS World University Rankings">QS World University Rankings</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-QS_133-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-QS-133">&#91;133&#93;</a></sup> It was ranked 44th in the world and 3rd in Canada by the 2019 <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education World University Rankings</a><sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_THES_W_134-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_THES_W-134">&#91;134&#93;</a></sup> and 70th in the world and 3rd in Canada by the <a href="/wiki/Academic_Ranking_of_World_Universities" title="Academic Ranking of World Universities">Academic Ranking of World Universities</a> (ARWU) 2018.<sup id="cite_ref-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W_131-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-USUnivRankings_ARWU_W-131">&#91;131&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Times_Higher_Education_World_University_Rankings" title="Times Higher Education World University Rankings">Times Higher Education</a> also ranked McGill 18th in the world in its 2017 Global University Employability Ranking.<sup id="cite_ref-UnivRankings_THES_GEUR_136-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UnivRankings_THES_GEUR-136">&#91;136&#93;</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Nature_(journal)" title="Nature (journal)">Nature</a></i> ranked McGill 70th in the world and 2nd in Canada among academic institutions for high-impact research in the 2018 edition of Nature Index.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">&#91;140&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>McGill is one of 26 members of the <a href="/wiki/Global_University_Leaders_Forum" title="Global University Leaders Forum">Global University Leaders Forum</a> (GULF), which acts as an intellectual community within the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> to advise its leadership on matters relating to higher education and research.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">&#91;141&#93;</a></sup> It is the only Canadian university member of GULF.<sup id="cite_ref-McGill_newsroom_9-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-McGill_newsroom-9">&#91;9&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><i><a href="/wiki/The_Globe_and_Mail" title="The Globe and Mail">The Globe and Mail</a></i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s Canadian University Report 2017 categorised McGill as "above average" for its bursaries and awards, research, and library resources, and as "average" for its student experience.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">&#91;142&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;"><a href="/wiki/File:89_virtualtourphase1_618.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/d7/89_virtualtourphase1_618.jpg/170px-89_virtualtourphase1_618.jpg" width="170" height="256" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/d/d7/89_virtualtourphase1_618.jpg 1.5x" data-file-width="239" data-file-height="360" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:89_virtualtourphase1_618.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Bronfman Building, part of the <a href="/wiki/Desautels_Faculty_of_Management" title="Desautels Faculty of Management">Desautels Faculty of Management</a></div></div></div>
<p>The <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i>, in its 2018 Global MBA ranking, placed <a href="/wiki/Desautels_Faculty_of_Management" title="Desautels Faculty of Management">Desautels Faculty of Management</a>'s MBA programme 78th in the world and 1st in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">&#91;143&#93;</a></sup> The ranking placed it 55th and 43rd worldwide in the value for money and alumni recommended categories respectively. The <i><a href="/wiki/Eduniversal" title="Eduniversal">Eduniversal</a></i> Ranking placed the Desautels Faculty of Management of McGill University first in Canada among business schools.<sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">&#91;144&#93;</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/BusinessWeek" class="mw-redirect" title="BusinessWeek">BusinessWeek</a>'s Best International Business Schools ranking 2017, Desautels was ranked 28th among international (non-U.S.) business schools.<sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">&#91;145&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Research Infosource ranked McGill 2nd in its 2017 edition of Canada's Top 50 Research Universities.<sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">&#91;146&#93;</a></sup> Research Infosource also ranked McGill 3rd in Canada for research income per faculty, and 3rd among Canadian medical/doctoral universities for research income growth.<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">&#91;147&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2017 Corporate Knights ranked McGill second in Canada in their Greenest Campuses in Canada index.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">&#91;148&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Research">Research</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Research">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_Ernest_Rutherfords_laboratory,_early_20th_century._(9660575343).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Sir_Ernest_Rutherfords_laboratory%2C_early_20th_century._%289660575343%29.jpg/220px-Sir_Ernest_Rutherfords_laboratory%2C_early_20th_century._%289660575343%29.jpg" width="220" height="163" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Sir_Ernest_Rutherfords_laboratory%2C_early_20th_century._%289660575343%29.jpg/330px-Sir_Ernest_Rutherfords_laboratory%2C_early_20th_century._%289660575343%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/97/Sir_Ernest_Rutherfords_laboratory%2C_early_20th_century._%289660575343%29.jpg/440px-Sir_Ernest_Rutherfords_laboratory%2C_early_20th_century._%289660575343%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1250" data-file-height="924" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Sir_Ernest_Rutherfords_laboratory,_early_20th_century._(9660575343).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The laboratory of Rutherford, early 20th century</div></div></div>
<p>Research plays a critical role at McGill. McGill is affiliated with 12 <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Laureate" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Laureate">Nobel Laureates</a> and professors have won major teaching prizes. According to the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_Universities_and_Colleges_of_Canada" class="mw-redirect" title="Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada">Association of Universities and Colleges of Canada</a>, "researchers at McGill are affiliated with about 75 major research centres and networks, and are engaged in an extensive array of research partnerships with other universities, government and industry in Quebec and Canada, throughout North America and in dozens of other countries."<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">&#91;149&#93;</a></sup> In 2016, McGill had over $547 million of sponsored research income, the second highest in Canada,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">&#91;150&#93;</a></sup> and a research intensity per faculty of $317,600, the third highest among full-service universities in Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">&#91;151&#93;</a></sup> McGill has one of the largest patent portfolios among Canadian universities.<sup id="cite_ref-research07-08_152-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-research07-08-152">&#91;152&#93;</a></sup> McGill's researchers are supported by the <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Library" title="McGill University Library">McGill University Library</a>, which comprises 13 branch libraries and holds over six million items.<sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">&#91;153&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Since 1926, McGill has been a member of the <a href="/wiki/Association_of_American_Universities" title="Association of American Universities">Association of American Universities</a> (AAU), an organization of leading research universities in North America. McGill is a founding member of <a href="/wiki/Universitas_21" title="Universitas 21">Universitas 21</a>, an international network of leading research-intensive universities that work together to expand their global reach and advance their plans for internationalization. 
McGill is one of 26 members of the prestigious <a href="/wiki/Global_University_Leaders_Forum" title="Global University Leaders Forum">Global University Leaders Forum</a> (GULF), which acts as an intellectual community within the <a href="/wiki/World_Economic_Forum" title="World Economic Forum">World Economic Forum</a> to advise its leadership on matters relating to higher education and research. It is the only Canadian university member of GULF. McGill is also a member of the <a href="/wiki/U15_(universities)" class="mw-redirect" title="U15 (universities)">U15</a>, a group of prominent research universities within Canada.
</p><p><a href="/wiki/McGill-Queen%27s_University_Press" title="McGill-Queen&#39;s University Press">McGill-Queen's University Press</a> began as McGill in 1963 and amalgamated with Queen's in 1969. McGill-Queen's University Press focuses on Canadian studies and publishes the Canadian Public Administration Series.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">&#91;154&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg/220px-Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg.png" width="220" height="237" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg/330px-Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/74/Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg/440px-Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="860" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Electron_shell_086_Radon.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Radon, discovered at McGill by physicist Ernest Rutherford</div></div></div>
<p>McGill is perhaps best recognized for its research and discoveries in the health sciences. <a href="/wiki/William_Osler" title="William Osler">Sir William Osler</a>, <a href="/wiki/Wilder_Penfield" title="Wilder Penfield">Wilder Penfield</a>, <a href="/wiki/Donald_Olding_Hebb" class="mw-redirect" title="Donald Olding Hebb">Donald Hebb</a>, <a href="/wiki/Brenda_Milner" title="Brenda Milner">Brenda Milner</a>, and others made significant discoveries in <a href="/wiki/Medicine" title="Medicine">medicine</a>, <a href="/wiki/Neuroscience" title="Neuroscience">neuroscience</a> and <a href="/wiki/Psychology" title="Psychology">psychology</a> while working at McGill, many at the University's <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Neurological_Institute" class="mw-redirect" title="Montreal Neurological Institute">Montreal Neurological Institute</a>. The first hormone governing the Immune System (later christened the Cytokine 'Interleukin-2') was discovered at McGill in 1965 by Gordon &amp; McLean.<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">&#91;155&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The invention of the world's first artificial cell was made by <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Chang" title="Thomas Chang">Thomas Chang</a> while an undergraduate student at the university.<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">&#91;156&#93;</a></sup> While chair of physics at McGill, nuclear physicist <a href="/wiki/Ernest_Rutherford" title="Ernest Rutherford">Ernest Rutherford</a> performed the experiment that led to the discovery of the alpha particle and its function in radioactive decay, which won him the Nobel Prize in Chemistry in 1908. Alumnus <a href="/wiki/Jack_W._Szostak" title="Jack W. Szostak">Jack W. Szostak</a> was awarded the 2009 Nobel Prize in medicine for discovering a key mechanism in the genetic operations of cells, an insight that has inspired new lines of research into cancer.
</p><p>William Chalmers invented <a href="/wiki/Poly(methyl_methacrylate)" title="Poly(methyl methacrylate)">Plexiglas</a> while a graduate student at McGill.<sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">&#91;157&#93;</a></sup> In computing, <a href="/wiki/MUSIC/SP" title="MUSIC/SP">MUSIC/SP</a>, software for mainframes once popular among universities and colleges around the world, was developed at McGill. A team also contributed to the development of <a href="/wiki/Archie_search_engine" title="Archie search engine">Archie</a>, a pre-<a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">WWW</a> search engine. A 3270 terminal emulator developed at McGill was commercialized and later sold to Hummingbird Software. A team has developed digital musical instruments in the form of prosthesis, called <a href="/w/index.php?title=Musical_Prostheses&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Musical Prostheses (page does not exist)">Musical Prostheses</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">&#91;158&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span id="Libraries.2C_archives_and_museums"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Libraries,_archives_and_museums">Libraries, archives and museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Libraries, archives and museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Falcon_-_1951_-_Robert_Tait_McKenzie_-_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/The_Falcon_-_1951_-_Robert_Tait_McKenzie_-_01.jpg/220px-The_Falcon_-_1951_-_Robert_Tait_McKenzie_-_01.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/The_Falcon_-_1951_-_Robert_Tait_McKenzie_-_01.jpg/330px-The_Falcon_-_1951_-_Robert_Tait_McKenzie_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2e/The_Falcon_-_1951_-_Robert_Tait_McKenzie_-_01.jpg/440px-The_Falcon_-_1951_-_Robert_Tait_McKenzie_-_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:The_Falcon_-_1951_-_Robert_Tait_McKenzie_-_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>The Falcon, a statue outside of the Humanities and Social Sciences Library, part of the McLennan–Redpath Library Complex</div></div></div>
<p>The <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Library" title="McGill University Library">McGill University Libraries</a>. The McGill University Library includes 13 branches or subject libraries including the Department of Rare Books &amp; Special Collections which holds about 350,000 items, including books, manuscripts, maps, prints, and a general rare book collection.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">&#91;159&#93;</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/Osler_Library_of_the_History_of_Medicine" title="Osler Library of the History of Medicine">Osler Library of the History of Medicine</a> is the largest medical history library in Canada and one of the most comprehensive in the world.
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_Wirth_Music_Building_-_01.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Elizabeth_Wirth_Music_Building_-_01.jpg/220px-Elizabeth_Wirth_Music_Building_-_01.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Elizabeth_Wirth_Music_Building_-_01.jpg/330px-Elizabeth_Wirth_Music_Building_-_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/87/Elizabeth_Wirth_Music_Building_-_01.jpg/440px-Elizabeth_Wirth_Music_Building_-_01.jpg 2x" data-file-width="4608" data-file-height="3456" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Elizabeth_Wirth_Music_Building_-_01.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Elizabeth Wirth Music Building, also a library, sits adjacent to the old Strathcona Music Building</div></div></div>
<p>The <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.archives.mcgill.ca/index.htm">McGill University Archives</a> – now administered as part of the McGill Library – houses official records of, or relating to, or people/activities connected with McGill University. The collection consists of manuscripts, texts, photographs, audio-visual material, architectural records, cartographic materials, prints and drawings, microforms and artifacts.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">&#91;160&#93;</a></sup> In 1962 F. Cyril James declared that the newly founded McGill University Archives (MUA), while concentrating on the institutional records of McGill, had the mandate to acquire private papers of former faculty members. In the 1990s drew back their acquisition scope and in 2004 new terms of reference on private acquisitions were introduced that included a wider McGill Community.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">&#91;161&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/Redpath_Museum" title="Redpath Museum">Redpath Museum</a> houses collections of interest to <a href="/wiki/Ethnology" title="Ethnology">ethnology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Biology" title="Biology">biology</a>, <a href="/wiki/Paleontology" title="Paleontology">paleontology</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Mineralogy" title="Mineralogy">mineralogy</a>/<a href="/wiki/Geology" title="Geology">geology</a>. Built in 1882, the Redpath is the oldest building in Canada built specifically to be a museum.<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">&#91;162&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The McGill Medical Museum catalogues, preserves, conserves and displays collections that documents the study and practice of medicine at McGill University and its associated teaching hospitals. The Medical museum features collections, individual specimens, artifacts, equipment log books/autopsy journals/paper materials and medical instruments and apparati, 25 wax models, 200 mostly skeletal dry specimens; and 400 lantern slides of anatomic specimens. There is a special emphasis on pathology; there are 2000 fluid filled-preserved anatomical and pathological specimens. The <a href="/wiki/Osler_Library_of_the_History_of_Medicine#Collection" title="Osler Library of the History of Medicine">Osler collection</a>, for example consists of 60 wet specimens while The Abbott collection consists of 80 wet specimens, mostly examples of congenital cardiac disease.<sup id="cite_ref-163" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-163">&#91;163&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_body">Student body</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Student body">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Proud_graduates.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Proud_graduates.jpg/220px-Proud_graduates.jpg" width="220" height="282" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Proud_graduates.jpg/330px-Proud_graduates.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4e/Proud_graduates.jpg/440px-Proud_graduates.jpg 2x" data-file-width="6592" data-file-height="8459" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Proud_graduates.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Ph.D. candidates march at Commencement in McGill's <a href="/wiki/Scarlet_(color)" title="Scarlet (color)">scarlet</a> regalia.<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">&#91;164&#93;</a></sup></div></div></div>
<p>McGill's student population includes 27,475 <a href="/wiki/Undergraduate" class="mw-redirect" title="Undergraduate">undergraduate</a> and 9,473 <a href="/wiki/Graduate_student" class="mw-redirect" title="Graduate student">graduate students</a> representing diverse geographic and linguistic backgrounds.<sup id="cite_ref-165" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-165">&#91;165&#93;</a></sup> Of the entire student population, 54.7% are from Quebec and 25.4% are from the rest of Canada, while 20.0% are from outside of Canada (including the United States). International students hail from about 150 different countries,<sup id="cite_ref-166" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-166">&#91;166&#93;</a></sup> with Americans comprising about half of all international undergraduates and a third of all international postgraduates in the entering class of 2010.<sup id="cite_ref-admissions_167-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-admissions-167">&#91;167&#93;</a></sup> Almost half of McGill students claim a first language other than English. While the university is located in a Francophone province, only 17.8% of the students claim French as their mother tongue, compared to 51.8% who claim English and 30.5% who claim some other language.<sup id="cite_ref-168" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-168">&#91;168&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_organizations">Student organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Student organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The campus has an active <a href="/wiki/Students%27_union" title="Students&#39; union">students' society</a> represented by the undergraduate <a href="/wiki/Students%27_Society_of_McGill_University" title="Students&#39; Society of McGill University">Students' Society of McGill University</a> (SSMU) and the <a href="/w/index.php?title=Post-Graduate_Students%27_Society_of_McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Post-Graduate Students&#39; Society of McGill University (page does not exist)">Post-Graduate Students' Society of McGill University</a> (PGSS). Due to the large postdoctoral student population, the PGSS also contains a semi-autonomous Association of Postdoctoral Fellows (APF). In addition, each faculty and department has its own student governing body, the largest faculty associations being the Arts Undergraduate Society (AUS) and the Science Undergraduate Society (SUS).<sup id="cite_ref-169" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-169">&#91;169&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-170" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-170">&#91;170&#93;</a></sup> The oldest is the Medical Students Society, founded in 1859.<sup id="cite_ref-171" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-171">&#91;171&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>There are hundreds of clubs and student organizations at the university. Many of them are centred around McGill's student union building, the University Centre. There are student-run teams located in the McConnell building such as the McGill Racing Team, McGill EV and McGill Baja. In 1992, students held a <a href="/wiki/Referendum" title="Referendum">referendum</a> which called for the University Centre to be named for actor and McGill alumnus <a href="/wiki/William_Shatner" title="William Shatner">William Shatner</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-172" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-172">&#91;172&#93;</a></sup> The university administration refused to accept the name and did not attend the opening. Traditionally, the administration names buildings in honour of deceased members of the university community or for major <a href="/wiki/Benefactor_(law)" title="Benefactor (law)">benefactors</a>—Shatner is neither.<sup id="cite_ref-173" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-173">&#91;173&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>McGill has a number of student-run publications. <i><a href="/wiki/The_McGill_Daily" title="The McGill Daily">The McGill Daily</a></i>, first published in 1911, was previously published twice weekly,<sup id="cite_ref-mcgdaily_174-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgdaily-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> but shifted to a once-a-week publication schedule in September 2013 due to tightened budgets.<sup id="cite_ref-175" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-175">&#91;175&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Le_D%C3%A9lit_fran%C3%A7ais" title="Le Délit français">Délit français</a></i> is the Daily's French-language counterpart. The combined circulation of both papers is over 28,000.<sup id="cite_ref-mcgdaily_174-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-mcgdaily-174">&#91;174&#93;</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/McGill_Tribune" title="McGill Tribune">McGill Tribune</a></i> currently publishes once a week, circulating approximately 11,000 copies across campus. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Bull_%26_Bear" title="The Bull &amp; Bear">The Bull &amp; Bear</a></i>, operating under the Management Undergraduate Society, publishes 1,000 copies each month.<sup id="cite_ref-bullandbear_176-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-bullandbear-176">&#91;176&#93;</a></sup> The satirical publication <i>Plumber's Faucet</i> and its counterpart <i>Plumber's Legder</i> (established in 2012) operate under the Engineering Undergraduate Society. Past publications include the <i>Red Herring</i> and the <i>Plumber's Pot</i>. <a href="/wiki/CKUT" class="mw-redirect" title="CKUT">CKUT</a> (90.3 FM) is the campus radio station. <a href="/wiki/TVMcGill" title="TVMcGill">TVMcGill</a> is the University TV station, broadcasting on closed-circuit television and over the internet.<sup id="cite_ref-177" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-177">&#91;177&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The <a href="/wiki/McGill_University_Faculty_of_Law" title="McGill University Faculty of Law">McGill University Faculty of Law</a> is home to three student-run academic journals, including the world-renowned <i><a href="/wiki/McGill_Law_Journal" title="McGill Law Journal">McGill Law Journal</a></i>, founded in 1952.<sup id="cite_ref-178" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-178">&#91;178&#93;</a></sup> Other student-run journals include such publications as the <i>McGill Journal of Law and Health,</i> the <i>McGill Journal of Medicine</i>, and the <i>McGill Journal of Education.</i>
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Opening_of_the_McGill_University_Student_Union_building,_Montreal,_QC,_1906.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Opening_of_the_McGill_University_Student_Union_building%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1906.jpg/220px-Opening_of_the_McGill_University_Student_Union_building%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1906.jpg" width="220" height="178" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Opening_of_the_McGill_University_Student_Union_building%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1906.jpg/330px-Opening_of_the_McGill_University_Student_Union_building%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1906.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/51/Opening_of_the_McGill_University_Student_Union_building%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1906.jpg/440px-Opening_of_the_McGill_University_Student_Union_building%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1906.jpg 2x" data-file-width="757" data-file-height="612" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Opening_of_the_McGill_University_Student_Union_building,_Montreal,_QC,_1906.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Opening of the Student Union building, 1906</div></div></div>
<p>While <a href="/wiki/Fraternities_and_sororities_in_North_America" class="mw-redirect" title="Fraternities and sororities in North America">fraternities and sororities</a> are not a large part of student life at McGill, some, including fraternities <a href="/wiki/Zeta_Psi" title="Zeta Psi">Zeta Psi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Kappa_Epsilon" title="Delta Kappa Epsilon">Delta Kappa Epsilon</a>, <a href="/w/index.php?title=Quebec_Alpha_%E2%80%93_Sigma_Alpha_Epsilon&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Quebec Alpha – Sigma Alpha Epsilon (page does not exist)">Sigma Alpha Epsilon</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Delta Phi">Alpha Delta Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Epsilon_Pi" title="Alpha Epsilon Pi">Alpha Epsilon Pi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-179" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-179">&#91;179&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Sigma_Phi" title="Alpha Sigma Phi">Alpha Sigma Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Delta_Lambda_Phi" title="Delta Lambda Phi">Delta Lambda Phi</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Society" title="Kappa Alpha Society">Kappa Alpha Society</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Chi" title="Sigma Chi">Sigma Chi</a> and sororities <a href="/wiki/Gamma_Phi_Beta" title="Gamma Phi Beta">Gamma Phi Beta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Kappa_Gamma" title="Kappa Kappa Gamma">Kappa Kappa Gamma</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kappa_Alpha_Theta" title="Kappa Alpha Theta">Kappa Alpha Theta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi" title="Alpha Phi">Alpha Phi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Omicron_Pi" title="Alpha Omicron Pi">Alpha Omicron Pi</a> have been established at the university. <a href="/wiki/Phi_Kappa_Pi" title="Phi Kappa Pi">Phi Kappa Pi</a>, Canada's only national fraternity, was founded at McGill and the University of Toronto in 1913 and continues to be active. With just over 2% of the student body population participating, involvement is below that of most American universities,<sup id="cite_ref-180" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-180">&#91;180&#93;</a></sup> but on par with most Canadian schools.
</p><p><i>Queer McGill</i> (formerly <i>Gay McGill</i>)<sup id="cite_ref-qrep_181-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-qrep-181">&#91;181&#93;</a></sup> has supported <a href="/wiki/Lesbian" title="Lesbian">lesbian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Bisexual" class="mw-redirect" title="Bisexual">bisexual</a>, <a href="/wiki/Gay" title="Gay">gay</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Transgender" title="Transgender">transgender</a> students since 1972.<sup id="cite_ref-Queer_McGill_182-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Queer_McGill-182">&#91;182&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Many large organizations, including <a href="/wiki/Non-governmental_organization" title="Non-governmental organization">NGOs</a>, have a local presence on campus. The International Relations Students Association of McGill (IRSAM) publishes the world's only all-inclusive international relations research journal, the <a href="/wiki/McGill_International_Review" title="McGill International Review">McGill International Review</a><sup id="cite_ref-IRSAM_183-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-IRSAM-183">&#91;183&#93;</a></sup> and currently has consultative status with the UN's <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Economic_and_Social_Council" title="United Nations Economic and Social Council">Economic and Social Council</a> (ECOSOC) and the <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Educational,_Scientific_and_Cultural_Organization" class="mw-redirect" title="United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization">United Nations Educational, Scientific and Cultural Organization</a> (UNESCO).<sup id="cite_ref-184" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-184">&#91;184&#93;</a></sup> Since 1990, IRSAM has hosted an annual <a href="/wiki/Model_United_Nations" title="Model United Nations">Model United Nations</a>, McMUN, for university students and since 1993 it has hosted an annual <a href="/wiki/Model_United_Nations" title="Model United Nations">Model United Nations</a>, SSUNS, for high school students. Other humanitarian groups represented at McGill include <a href="/wiki/UNICEF" title="UNICEF">UNICEF</a>, <a href="/wiki/Oxfam" title="Oxfam">Oxfam</a>, <a href="/wiki/End_Poverty_Now" title="End Poverty Now">End Poverty Now</a>, <a href="/wiki/Right_to_Play" class="mw-redirect" title="Right to Play">Right to Play</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Free_the_Children" class="mw-redirect" title="Free the Children">Free the Children</a>.
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Montreal_021.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Montreal_021.jpg/220px-Montreal_021.jpg" width="220" height="166" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Montreal_021.jpg/330px-Montreal_021.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/da/Montreal_021.jpg/440px-Montreal_021.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1632" data-file-height="1232" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Montreal_021.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>McGill's Molson Stadium</div></div></div>
<p>McGill is represented in <a href="/wiki/U_Sports" title="U Sports">U Sports</a> by the <a href="/wiki/McGill_Redmen" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill Redmen">McGill Redmen</a> (men's) and the <a href="/wiki/McGill_Martlets" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill Martlets">McGill Martlets</a> (women's). Following a major restructuring of the varsity programme for the fall semester of 2010, McGill is currently home to 28 varsity teams. McGill is known for its strong hockey and lacrosse programs.<sup id="cite_ref-185" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-185">&#91;185&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-186" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-186">&#91;186&#93;</a></sup> McGill's unique mascot, Marty the <a href="/wiki/Martlet" title="Martlet">Martlet</a>, was introduced during the 2005 Homecoming game.<sup id="cite_ref-187" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-187">&#91;187&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The downtown McGill campus sport and exercise facilities include: the McGill Sports Centre (which includes the Tomlinson Fieldhouse and the Windsor Varsity Clinic),<sup id="cite_ref-188" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-188">&#91;188&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Percival_Molson_Memorial_Stadium" title="Percival Molson Memorial Stadium">Molson Stadium</a>, Memorial Pool, Tomlinson Hall, McConnell Arena, Forbes Field, many outdoor <a href="/wiki/Tennis_courts" class="mw-redirect" title="Tennis courts">tennis courts</a> and other <a href="/wiki/Extra-curricular" class="mw-redirect" title="Extra-curricular">extra-curricular</a> <a href="/wiki/Arena" title="Arena">arenas</a> and faculties.<sup id="cite_ref-189" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-189">&#91;189&#93;</a></sup> The Macdonald Campus facilities, include an arena, a <a href="/wiki/Gym" title="Gym">gymnasium</a>, a <a href="/wiki/Swimming_pool" title="Swimming pool">pool</a>, tennis courts, <a href="/wiki/Fitness_centre" class="mw-redirect" title="Fitness centre">fitness centres</a> and hundreds of acres of green space for regular use.<sup id="cite_ref-190" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-190">&#91;190&#93;</a></sup> The university's largest sporting venue, Molson Stadium, was constructed in 1914. Following an expansion project completed in 2010, it now seats just over 25,000,<sup id="cite_ref-191" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-191">&#91;191&#93;</a></sup> and is the current home field of the <a href="/wiki/Montreal_Alouettes" title="Montreal Alouettes">Montreal Alouettes</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-192" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-192">&#91;192&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletic_history">Athletic history</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Athletic history">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_hockey_match.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/McGill_hockey_match.jpg/220px-McGill_hockey_match.jpg" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/McGill_hockey_match.jpg/330px-McGill_hockey_match.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/26/McGill_hockey_match.jpg/440px-McGill_hockey_match.jpg 2x" data-file-width="608" data-file-height="471" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_hockey_match.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>A hockey match at McGill in 1901</div></div></div>
<p>In 1868, the first recorded game of <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby</a> in North America occurred in Montreal, between British army officers and McGill students,<sup id="cite_ref-193" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-193">&#91;193&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-194" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-194">&#91;194&#93;</a></sup> giving McGill the oldest university-affiliated rugby club in North America. Other McGill-originated sports evolved out of rugby rules: football, hockey, and basketball. The first game of North American <a href="/wiki/Gridiron_football" title="Gridiron football">football</a> was played between McGill and <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard</a> on May 14, 1874,<sup id="cite_ref-195" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-195">&#91;195&#93;</a></sup> leading to the spread of American football throughout the Ivy League.<sup id="cite_ref-196" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-196">&#91;196&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>On March 3, 1875, the <a href="/wiki/First_indoor_hockey_game" class="mw-redirect" title="First indoor hockey game">first organized indoor</a> <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">hockey</a> game was played at Montreal's <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Skating_Rink" title="Victoria Skating Rink">Victoria Skating Rink</a> between two nine-player teams, including <a href="/wiki/James_Creighton_(ice_hockey)" title="James Creighton (ice hockey)">James Creighton</a> and several McGill University students. The <a href="/wiki/McGill_Redmen" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill Redmen">McGill University Hockey Club</a>, the first organized hockey club, was founded in 1877<sup id="cite_ref-197" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-197">&#91;197&#93;</a></sup> and played its first game on January 31, 1877.<sup id="cite_ref-198" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-198">&#91;198&#93;</a></sup> Very soon thereafter, those McGill students wrote the first hockey rule book. A McGill team was one of four that competed in the <a href="/wiki/Amateur_Hockey_Association_of_Canada" title="Amateur Hockey Association of Canada">Amateur Hockey Association of Canada</a>, founded in 1886. AHAC teams competed for the first <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Cup" title="Stanley Cup">Stanley Cup</a> in 1893; the AHAC became one of predecessor organizations of the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-Lennox2009_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Lennox2009-20">&#91;20&#93;</a></sup> McGill alumnus <a href="/wiki/James_Naismith" title="James Naismith">James Naismith</a> invented basketball in early December 1891.<sup id="cite_ref-199" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-199">&#91;199&#93;</a></sup> Norwegian <a href="/wiki/Herman_Smith-Johannsen" title="Herman Smith-Johannsen">Herman "Jackrabbit" Smith-Johannsen</a> (later the coach of Canada's 1932 Olympic team) popularized <a href="/wiki/Cross-country_skiing" title="Cross-country skiing">cross-country skiing</a> in North America from McGill's Gault Estate in Mont St. Hilaire.
</p><p>There has been a McGill alumnus or alumna competing at every <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic Games</a> since 1908.<sup id="cite_ref-200" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-200">&#91;200&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-201" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-201">&#91;201&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-202" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-202">&#91;202&#93;</a></sup> Swimmer <a href="/wiki/George_Hodgson" title="George Hodgson">George Hodgson</a> won two gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/1912_Summer_Olympics" title="1912 Summer Olympics">1912 Summer Olympics</a>, ice hockey goaltender <a href="/wiki/Kim_St-Pierre" title="Kim St-Pierre">Kim St-Pierre</a> won gold medals at the <a href="/wiki/2002_Winter_Olympics" title="2002 Winter Olympics">2002 Winter Olympics</a> and at the <a href="/wiki/2006_Winter_Olympics" title="2006 Winter Olympics">2006 Winter Olympics</a>. Other 2006 gold medalists are <a href="/wiki/Jennifer_Heil" title="Jennifer Heil">Jennifer Heil</a> (women's freestyle mogul) and goaltender <a href="/wiki/Charline_Labont%C3%A9" title="Charline Labonté">Charline Labonté</a> (women's ice hockey).
</p>
<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_Hockey_Team,_Montreal,_QC,_1904.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/McGill_Hockey_Team%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1904.jpg/220px-McGill_Hockey_Team%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1904.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/McGill_Hockey_Team%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1904.jpg/330px-McGill_Hockey_Team%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1904.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/McGill_Hockey_Team%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1904.jpg/440px-McGill_Hockey_Team%2C_Montreal%2C_QC%2C_1904.jpg 2x" data-file-width="766" data-file-height="576" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:McGill_Hockey_Team,_Montreal,_QC,_1904.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>McGill Hockey Team, 1904</div></div></div>
<p>In 1996, the McGill Sports <a href="/wiki/Hall_of_Fame" class="mw-redirect" title="Hall of Fame">Hall of Fame</a> was established to honour its best student athletes. Notable members of the Hall of Fame include <a href="/wiki/James_Naismith" title="James Naismith">James Naismith</a> and <a href="/wiki/Sydney_David_Pierce" title="Sydney David Pierce">Sydney Pierce</a>.
</p><p>A 2005 <a href="/wiki/Hazing" title="Hazing">hazing</a> scandal forced the cancellation of the final two games in the McGill Redmen football season.
</p><p>In 2006, McGill's Senate approved a proposed anti-hazing policy to define forbidden initiation practices.<sup id="cite_ref-203" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-203">&#91;203&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Fight_song">Fight song</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Fight song">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p><i>The McGill University song book,</i> compiled by a committee of graduates and undergraduates, was published in Montreal by W.F. Brown, circa 1896.<sup id="cite_ref-204" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-204">&#91;204&#93;</a></sup>
Notable among a number of songs commonly played and sung at various events such as <a href="/wiki/Graduation" title="Graduation">commencement</a> and <a href="/wiki/Convocation" title="Convocation">convocation</a>, and athletic games are:
</p>
<ul><li>"Alma Mater McGill," with words by J. McDougall;</li>
<li>"L'Enfant du McGill," with words by Louis-Honoré Fréchette, and music by Guillaume Couture;</li>
<li>"God Save McGill," with words by W.M. Mackeracher, tune 'God Save the Queen';</li>
<li>"A Health to Old McGill," with words by R.W. Huntingdon, and music by Mrs W.C. Baynes;</li>
<li>"McGill," with words by C.W. Colby, sung to the tune 'The Gay Cavalier';</li>
<li>"McGill Revisited," with words by John Cox,</li>
<li>"McGill Students," with words by W.N. Evans;</li>
<li>"The Student of McGill," with words by R.D. McGibbon<sup id="cite_ref-205" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-205">&#91;205&#93;</a></sup></li></ul>
<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>
<p>McGill maintains an academic and athletic rivalry with <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University" title="Queen&#39;s University">Queen's University</a> in <a href="/wiki/Kingston,_Ontario" title="Kingston, Ontario">Kingston, Ontario</a>. Competition between rowing athletes at the two schools has inspired an annual boat race between the two universities in the spring of each year since 1997, inspired by the famous <a href="/wiki/The_Boat_Race" title="The Boat Race">Oxford-Cambridge Boat Race</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-206" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-206">&#91;206&#93;</a></sup> The football rivalry, which started in 1884, ended after Canadian university athletic divisions were re-organized in 2000; the Ontario-Quebec Intercollegiate Football Conference was divided into <a href="/wiki/Ontario_University_Athletics" title="Ontario University Athletics">Ontario University Athletics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Quebec_Student_Sports_Federation" class="mw-redirect" title="Quebec Student Sports Federation">Quebec Student Sports Federation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-207" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-207">&#91;207&#93;</a></sup> The rivalry returned in 2002 when it transferred to the annual home-and-home hockey games between the two institutions. Queen's students refer to these matches as "Kill McGill" games, and usually show up in Montreal in atypically large numbers to cheer on the <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_Golden_Gaels" title="Queen&#39;s Golden Gaels">Queen's Golden Gaels</a> hockey team.<sup id="cite_ref-208" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-208">&#91;208&#93;</a></sup> In 2007, McGill students arrived in bus-loads to cheer on the <a href="/wiki/McGill_Redmen" class="mw-redirect" title="McGill Redmen">McGill Redmen</a>, occupying a third of Queen's Jock Harty Arena.<sup id="cite_ref-209" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-209">&#91;209&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>The school also competes in the annual "<a href="/wiki/Old_Four" title="Old Four">Old Four (IV)</a>" soccer tournament, with <a href="/wiki/Queen%27s_University" title="Queen&#39;s University">Queen's University</a>, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Toronto" title="University of Toronto">University of Toronto</a> and the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Western_Ontario" title="University of Western Ontario">University of Western Ontario</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-210" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-210">&#91;210&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>McGill and <a href="/wiki/Harvard" class="mw-redirect" title="Harvard">Harvard</a> are also athletic rivals, as demonstrated by the biennial Harvard-McGill rugby games, alternately played in Montreal and Cambridge.<sup id="cite_ref-211" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-211">&#91;211&#93;</a></sup>
</p>
<ul class="gallery mw-gallery-traditional">
		<li class="gallerybox" style="width: 155px"><div style="width: 155px">
