<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Historical_links">Historical links</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Historical links">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<ul><li>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Glasgow" title="University of Glasgow">University of Glasgow</a>, one of four <a href="/wiki/Ancient_universities_of_Scotland" title="Ancient universities of Scotland">ancient Scottish universities</a> and member of the British <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a>. Founded in 1451, the original benefactor of McGill College, James McGill, studied here in the 1750s<sup id="cite_ref-212" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-212">&#91;212&#93;</a></sup> before his family worked as merchants in the city.<sup id="cite_ref-213" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-213">&#91;213&#93;</a></sup> The two universities continue this link today as part of <a href="/wiki/Universitas_21" title="Universitas 21">Universitas 21</a>, an international student exchange programme.</li>
<li>The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Edinburgh" title="University of Edinburgh">University of Edinburgh</a>, one of four <a href="/wiki/Ancient_universities_of_Scotland" title="Ancient universities of Scotland">ancient Scottish universities</a> and member of the British <a href="/wiki/Russell_Group" title="Russell Group">Russell Group</a>. The University was founded as a civic institution in 1583 and has maintained a strong reputation in the study of medicine, among other disciplines. McGill's first (and, for several years, its only) faculty, Medicine, was founded by four physicians/surgeons who had trained in Edinburgh.<sup id="cite_ref-214" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-214">&#91;214&#93;</a></sup> In common with Glasgow, Edinburgh shares an international exchange link with McGill through <a href="/wiki/Universitas_21" title="Universitas 21">Universitas 21</a>.</li></ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_people">Notable people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=McGill_University&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Notable people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_McGill_University_people" title="List of McGill University people">List of McGill University people</a></div>
<p>In the arts, McGill students include four <a href="/wiki/Pulitzer_Prize" title="Pulitzer Prize">Pulitzer Prize</a> winners,<sup id="cite_ref-PP1_16-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PP1-16">&#91;16&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PP2_17-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PP2-17">&#91;17&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PP3_215-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PP3-215">&#91;215&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-PP4_216-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-PP4-216">&#91;216&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Templeton_Prize" title="Templeton Prize">Templeton</a> and <a href="/wiki/Berggruen_Prize_for_Philosophy" class="mw-redirect" title="Berggruen Prize for Philosophy">Berggruen</a> Prize winner <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taylor_(philosopher)" title="Charles Taylor (philosopher)">Charles Taylor</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-217" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-217">&#91;217&#93;</a></sup> essayist and novelist <a href="/wiki/John_Ralston_Saul" title="John Ralston Saul">John Ralston Saul</a>, a Companion of the Order of Canada along with Charles Taylor, <a href="/wiki/Juno_Award" title="Juno Award">Juno Award</a> winners <a href="/wiki/Sam_Roberts" title="Sam Roberts">Sam Roberts</a> and <a href="/wiki/Donald_Steven" title="Donald Steven">Donald Steven</a>, singer-songwriter Prita Chhabra and <a href="/wiki/William_Shatner" title="William Shatner">William Shatner</a>, best known for his portrayal of <a href="/wiki/James_T._Kirk" title="James T. Kirk">Captain Kirk</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Star_Trek" title="Star Trek">Star Trek</a></i> and winner of several <a href="/wiki/Emmy_Awards" class="mw-redirect" title="Emmy Awards">Emmy Awards</a>. Nine <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Academy Award">Academy Award</a> winners studied at McGill.<sup id="cite_ref-218" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-218">&#91;218&#93;</a></sup> Poet and singer-songwriter <a href="/wiki/Leonard_Cohen" title="Leonard Cohen">Leonard Cohen</a> majored in English at McGill and graduated in 1955.<sup id="cite_ref-219" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-219">&#91;219&#93;</a></sup> Composer and six-time Grammy award winner <a href="/wiki/Burt_Bacharach" title="Burt Bacharach">Burt Bacharach</a> studied music at McGill, and <a href="/wiki/Win_Butler" title="Win Butler">Win Butler</a> and <a href="/wiki/R%C3%A9gine_Chassagne" title="Régine Chassagne">Régine Chassagne</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Grammy_Award" title="Grammy Award">Grammy Award</a> winning group <a href="/wiki/Arcade_Fire" title="Arcade Fire">Arcade Fire</a> met while studying at McGill.<sup id="cite_ref-220" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-220">&#91;220&#93;</a></sup> 
In the sciences, students include doctors, inventors, five astronauts (out of 14 total selected in the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_Space_Agency" title="Canadian Space Agency">CSA</a>'s history)<sup id="cite_ref-221" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-221">&#91;221&#93;</a></sup> and scientist <a href="/wiki/Mark_J._Poznansky" title="Mark J. Poznansky">Mark J. Poznansky</a>, a member of the Order of Canada.<sup id="cite_ref-222" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-222">&#91;222&#93;</a></sup> On October 16, 2009, the 42nd American president, Bill Clinton accepted an Honorary Doctorate from McGill University.<sup id="cite_ref-223" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-223">&#91;223&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Some politicians and government officials both within Canada and abroad are McGill alumni, including three <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Canada" title="Prime Minister of Canada">Canadian prime ministers</a>, the incumbent <a href="/wiki/Governor_General_of_Canada" title="Governor General of Canada">Governor General of Canada</a>, and 14 justices of the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Canada" title="Supreme Court of Canada">Supreme Court of Canada</a>.  <a href="/wiki/Daniel_Oduber_Quir%C3%B3s" title="Daniel Oduber Quirós">Daniel Oduber Quirós</a> earned his degree in philosophy at McGill in 1948 and became president of <a href="/wiki/Costa_Rica" title="Costa Rica">Costa Rica</a> from 1974-1979.  <a href="/wiki/Vaira_V%C4%AB%C4%B7e-Freiberga" title="Vaira Vīķe-Freiberga">Vaira Vīķe-Freiberga</a> completed her Ph.D. at McGill and was elected as president of the <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Latvia" class="mw-redirect" title="Republic of Latvia">Republic of Latvia</a> in 1999, serving until 2007, as the first female president in Eastern Europe after Turkey's <a href="/wiki/Tansu_%C3%87iller" title="Tansu Çiller">Tansu Çiller</a>.   <a href="/wiki/Ahmed_Nazif" title="Ahmed Nazif">Ahmed Nazif</a> also completed a Ph.D. at McGill in 1983 and has served as the youngest <a href="/wiki/Prime_minister" title="Prime minister">prime minister</a> of <a href="/wiki/Egypt" title="Egypt">Egypt</a> since the republic's founding in 1953. <a href="/wiki/Zbigniew_Brzezinski" title="Zbigniew Brzezinski">Zbigniew Brzezinski</a>, former United States National Security Advisor under President Jimmy Carter completed both his B.A. and M.A. degrees at McGill in 1949 and 1950, respectively.
</p><p>In the <a href="/wiki/Canadian_federal_election,_2015" title="Canadian federal election, 2015">2015 Canadian election</a>, a total of twenty-five former McGill students were elected as Members of Parliament, including the current Prime Minister of Canada, <a href="/wiki/Justin_Trudeau" title="Justin Trudeau">Justin Trudeau</a> and three cabinet members.<sup id="cite_ref-224" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-224">&#91;224&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-225" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-225">&#91;225&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p>Corporate leaders and <a href="/wiki/Media_personalities" class="mw-redirect" title="Media personalities">media personalities</a> have also studied at McGill. Leading Canadian philanthropist and entrepreneur <a href="/wiki/Seymour_Schulich" title="Seymour Schulich">Seymour Schulich</a> donated $20 million, the highest donation to any music school in Canada, to the newly named <a href="/wiki/Schulich_School_of_Music" title="Schulich School of Music">Schulich School of Music</a>. <a href="/wiki/Henry_Mintzberg" title="Henry Mintzberg">Henry Mintzberg</a>, a professor at McGill's <a href="/wiki/Desautels_Faculty_of_Management" title="Desautels Faculty of Management">Desautels Faculty of Management</a> is an acclaimed management thinker and contributes to <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Economist" title="The Economist">The Economist</a></i>. Mintzberg is an Officer of the Order of Canada. Co-founder and president of <a href="/wiki/Matrox" title="Matrox">Matrox Electronic Systems Ltd.</a>, which innovates globally in graphics, video editing, and image processing, <a href="/wiki/Lorne_Trottier" title="Lorne Trottier">Lorne Trottier</a>, after whom the new engineering building is named, has donated $10 million towards services in information and technology at McGill. Media magnate <a href="/wiki/Conrad_Black" title="Conrad Black">Conrad Black</a> also studied at McGill.
</p><p>McGill students are also recognized as athletes, including various members of <a href="/wiki/Canadian_National_Team_(disambiguation)" class="mw-redirect mw-disambig" title="Canadian National Team (disambiguation)">Canadian national teams</a> and twenty-eight <a href="/wiki/Olympic_Games" title="Olympic Games">Olympic</a> medalists. Since the Olympics began, McGill has produced 112 Olympians who have won a total of eight gold medals, nine silver, and eleven bronze.<sup id="cite_ref-226" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-226">&#91;226&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-227" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-227">&#91;227&#93;</a></sup> From Pakistan, 2015 graduate Zohaib Asad Syed was the first student in the world at McGill with a world record number of 28 A grades in international O/IGCSE level exams along with University of Cambridge Top in the Region awards in O level Human and Social Biology, AS level General Paper, and was awarded with a cash prize of 1 million PKR by the then Prime Minister of Pakistan Yousaf Raza Gillani, he was also recognized and applauded by the principal and vice chancellor of McGill university Heather Munroe Blum in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-228" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-228">&#91;228&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-229" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-229">&#91;229&#93;</a></sup>
</p><p><a href="/wiki/Jacob_Viner" title="Jacob Viner">Jacob Viner</a>, who would later go on to form the beginnings of the modern day <a href="/wiki/Chicago_School_of_Economics" class="mw-redirect" title="Chicago School of Economics">Chicago School of Economics</a>, earned his undergraduate degree from McGill. <a href="/wiki/William_Osler" title="William Osler">William Osler</a>, one of the founders of the <a href="/wiki/Johns_Hopkins_School_of_Medicine" title="Johns Hopkins School of Medicine">Johns Hopkins School of Medicine</a>, and the originator of the concept of <a href="/wiki/Residency_(medicine)" title="Residency (medicine)">medical residency</a>, received his medical degree from McGill.
</p><p>Professors at McGill have won 26 <a href="/wiki/Prix_du_Qu%C3%A9bec" title="Prix du Québec">Prix du Québec</a>, 14 Prix de l'<a href="/wiki/Association_francophone_pour_le_savoir" title="Association francophone pour le savoir">Association francophone pour le savoir</a> and 21 <a href="/wiki/Isaak-Walton-Killam_Award" class="mw-redirect" title="Isaak-Walton-Killam Award">Killam Prizes</a>. Twelve <a href="/wiki/Nobel_Laureates" class="mw-redirect" title="Nobel Laureates">Nobel Laureates</a> have studied or taught at McGill, among them <a href="/wiki/Otto_Hahn" title="Otto Hahn">Otto Hahn</a>, who was awarded the 1944 Nobel Prize in Chemistry for his discovery of the <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_fission" title="Nuclear fission">nuclear fission</a> of uranium and thorium.
</p><p>Since 1902, Canadian undergraduate students have been eligible for Rhodes Scholarships to study at the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Oxford" title="University of Oxford">University of Oxford</a>. Since then, McGill students have won 142 Rhodes Scholarships – more than any other Canadian University.<sup id="cite_ref-rhodes_230-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rhodes-230">&#91;230&#93;</a></sup> These students include parliamentary and cabinet ministers <a href="/wiki/David_Lewis_(politician)" title="David Lewis (politician)">David Lewis</a> (1932), <a href="/wiki/Alastair_Gillespie" title="Alastair Gillespie">Alastair Gillespie</a> (1947), and <a href="/wiki/Marcel_Mass%C3%A9" title="Marcel Massé">Marcel Massé</a> (1963), and political philosopher <a href="/wiki/Charles_Taylor_(philosopher)" title="Charles Taylor (philosopher)">Charles Taylor</a> (1952).
</p>
